Al-Quran as Source

Muhkam and Muhkam Bih: The Quran's Firmness and Its Role in Beliefs
Explaining the concepts of muhkam and muhkam bih and resolving the issue of proof for beliefs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muhkam and muhkam bih in Hanafi usul and explain how the Quran validates both rationally and transmittedly derived beliefs.

Core Idea
The Quran is muhkam in meaning and word; beliefs, though proven by reason, are valid only when they conform to the Quran.

In this passage, the commentator explores the relationship between the Quran's firmness (ihkam) and the beliefs (aqa'id) of Islam. A common objection arises: if beliefs are rationally established, how can the Quran make them firm? The Hanafi response clarifies that the Quran's role is not to originate proof for every belief but to confirm and validate them, ensuring they align with revelation. This lesson dissects the terms muhkam and muhkam bih and resolves the tension between rational and transmitted proofs.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish muhkam from muhkam bih
Recognize that muhkam refers to the firmness of meanings, while muhkam bih refers to the words that convey those meanings. This resolves an apparent redundancy.
The same entity (the Quran) is muhkam in one aspect and muhkam bih in another.
2
Understand the objection about beliefs
The objection states that beliefs are proven by reason, so the Quran cannot be their source. Note that the commentator uses 'ahkama' (made firm) not 'athbata' (proved).
The objection conflates proof (thubut) with firmness/validity (ihkam).
3
Apply the distinction between thubut and i'tibar
Some beliefs (like beatific vision) are transmitted, but even rational beliefs must conform to the Quran to be considered valid. Thus the Quran validates beliefs.
Thubut = source of proof; i'tibar = condition for validity.
4
Analyze the dual meanings of usul and furu'
The passage offers two interpretations: usul as universal proofs and furu' as rulings; or usul as beliefs and furu' as righteous deeds. This shows the flexibility of the Hanafi framework.
Each interpretation leads to different implications for what the Quran 'makes firm'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتھ اللہ تعالی نے اپنی کتاب کو محکم کیا ہے تو کتاب محکم اور صفت اعجاز محکم یہ ہے محکم اور محکم بہ شی ء واحد ہیں لیکن باعتبارین مختلفين فلا اشکال : الجواب (۲) توجیہ ثانی یہ ہے کہ محکم معانی ہیں اور محکم بہ الفاظ میں مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ اللہ تعالی نے الفاظ کے ذریعہ سے معانی قرآن پاک کو محکم اور پختہ کر دیا احتمال ثانی کے مطابق اگر اصول سے عقائد مراد ہوں تو مقصد ہوگا اللہ تعالی نے اپنی کتاب کے ذریعہ سے عقائد کو پختہ کر دیا احکام سے مراد ہو گا عقائد کی تائید و توثیق کرنا۔ سوال: عقائد کا ثبوت کتاب اللہ سے تو نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دلائل عقلیہ سے ہوتا ہے کیونکہ خود کتاب اللہ کا ثبوت موقوف ہے عقائد پر کتاب اللہ کا کتاب ہونا وہی تسلیم کرے گا جو وجود باری تعالی وصفات کا قائل ہوگا لھذ اشارح کا قول کہ ذات باری تعالی نے عقائد دینیہ کو کتاب کے ذریعہ سے محکم کر دیا درست نہیں: الجواب : (1) تسلیم ہے کہ بعض عقائد کا اثبات دلائل عقلیہ سے ہے لیکن بعض عقائد کا اثبات وائل نقلیہ سے ہے جیسے رویہ باری تعالی معاد جسمانی عذاب قبر۔ یہاں سے یہی عقائد مراد ہیں الجواب: (۲) جتنے عقائد میں خواہ ان کا اثبات دلائل عقلیہ سے ہو یا دلائل نقلیہ سے وہ معتد بھا اور صحیح تب ہونگے جب کتاب اللہ کیموافق ہوں تو من حیث الثبوت عقائد اگر چه موقوف على الكتاب نہیں لیکن من حیث الاعتداد والصحة موقوف على الكتاب ہیں بائیں اعتبار کتاب اللہ سے ان کا احکام ہو گا اسی بنیاد پر شارح کے احکم کا لفظ اختیار فرمایا البت کا لفظ ذکر نہیں فرمایا ( حاشیہ نمبر ایک صفحہ نمبر ۲ ۳ دیکھیں فروع میں بھی دو احتمال ہیں (۱) اگر اصول سے ادلہ کلیہ مراد ہوں تو فروع سے احکام مراد ہو نگے اگر اصول سے عقائد مراد ہوں تو فروع سے اعمال صالحہ مراد ہوں گے اگر اول مراد ہوں تو مقصد ہوگا اللہ تعالی نے اپنے خطاب کے ذریعہ سے ملتہ حنفیہ کے احکام کے مرتبہ وشان کو بلند کر دیا رفع سے مراد اعلاء قد ر ومرتبہ ہوگا اگر ثانی احتمال مراد ہو تو مقصد ہوگا اللہ تعالی نے اپنے خطاب کے ذریعہ سے شریعہ حنفیہ سہلہ کے اعمال صالحہ کو شرف قبولیت عطا کر کے ان کے مرتبے کو بلند کر دیا رفع سے مراد قبولیت ہو گا۔
Along with that, Allah has made His book muhkam (firm). So the book is muhkam and the attribute of inimitability is muhkam. This is that muhkam and muhkam bih are one thing, but from two different perspectives, so there is no problem. The second answer: The second explanation is that muhkam refers to meanings and muhkam bih refers to words. The purpose would be that Allah made the meanings of the Holy Qur'an firm and strong through words. According to the second probability, if by 'principles' (usul) are meant beliefs, then the purpose would be that Allah strengthened the beliefs through His book. And by 'rulings' (ahkam) would mean supporting and confirming beliefs. Question: The proof of beliefs is not from the Book of Allah but rather from rational proofs, because the proof of the Book of Allah itself depends on beliefs. Only he who believes in the existence and attributes of Allah will accept the Book of Allah as a book. Therefore, the statement of the commentator that Allah made religious beliefs firm through the book is not correct. Answer (1): It is conceded that the proof of some beliefs is from rational proofs, but the proof of some beliefs is from transmitted proofs, such as the beatific vision, bodily resurrection, punishment of the grave. Here, these beliefs are meant. Answer (2): All beliefs, whether their proof is from rational proofs or transmitted proofs, they will be valid and correct only when they agree with the Book of Allah. So, from the perspective of proof, beliefs are not dependent on the Book, but from the perspective of validity and correctness, they are dependent on the Book. In this sense, the Book of Allah has a ruling over them. On this basis, the commentator chose the word 'ahkama' and did not mention the word 'athbata'. (See footnote number 1, page 23). Regarding branches (furu') also, there are two probabilities: (1) If by 'principles' are meant universal proofs, then by 'branches' are meant rulings. (2) If by 'principles' are meant beliefs, then by 'branches' are meant righteous deeds. If the first is meant, then the purpose would be that Allah elevated the rank and status of the rulings of the Hanafi nation through His address. 'Rafa' (elevation) means exaltation of rank and status. If the second probability is meant, then the purpose would be that Allah elevated the rank of the righteous deeds of the easy Hanafi sharia by granting them the honor of acceptance through His address. 'Rafa' means acceptance.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the terms muhkam and muhkam bih from a Hanafi usul perspective. The commentator addresses a potential confusion: if both the Quran and its miracle are called muhkam, they are the same in essence but differ in aspect (one as object, the other as attribute). The main issue arises with a question: if beliefs (aqa'id) are proven by rational proofs, how can the Quran make them firm? The answer distinguishes between proof (thubut) and validity (i'tibar). Some beliefs (e.g., beatific vision, resurrection) are known only through transmitted proofs. Moreover, even rationally proven beliefs must agree with the Quran to be considered valid. Thus, the Quran's role is to confirm and validate, not necessarily to originate proof. This shows the Hanafi method of integrating rational and revealed sources. The passage also discusses the terms 'usul' and 'furu'' in two senses: either universal proofs and rulings, or beliefs and deeds. This flexibility allows the same framework to address both theological and legal branches.

Key Terms
محکم (muhkam): That which is made firm; in this context, refers to the Quran's meanings (the first answer) or the attribute of miraculousness (the second).
محکم بہ (muhkam bih): That by which something is made firm; here, it refers to the Quranic words that convey the meanings.
عقائد (aqa'id): Beliefs; here they include both rationally and transmittedly known tenets.
اصول (usul): Either universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah) or beliefs (aqa'id).
فروع (furu'): Either rulings (ahkam) or righteous deeds (a'mal salihah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the commentator's statement that Allah made religious beliefs firm through the book considered correct despite the objection?
A) Because all beliefs are proven by transmitted proofs from the Quran.
B) Because even rationally proven beliefs must conform to the Quran to be valid.
C) Because the Quran is the only source of belief.
D) Because the commentator did not use the word 'thubut' but 'ihkam'.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is muhkam in meaning and word; it validates beliefs by confirming their agreement with revelation, even when their proof is rational.

The Good Tree Simile: Principles and Branches in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the Quranic simile of the good tree and its application to principles and branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of the good tree simile and apply Taftazani's branching to show the dependency of branches on principles.

Core Idea
The good tree simile teaches that strong principles yield strong branches — faith and deeds are interdependent in Hanafi thought.

The Quran presents a profound simile of a good tree whose root is firm and whose branches reach the sky. In Hanafi usul, this simile is unpacked to illustrate the relationship between foundational principles (usul) and derived rulings (furu'). This lesson will walk you through the commentator's lexical analysis and Taftazani's systematic branching, showing how creed and law interlock.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic Simile and Its Components
Locate the verse (Surah Ibrahim:24-25) and list the four elements: kalimah (word of tawhid), asas (foundation/faith), rusukh (firmness), shumukh (loftiness). Understand the literal meaning of each in the context of the date palm.
The verse is cited as a basis for linking beliefs to actions.
2
Unpack the Commentator's Lexical Breakdown
Follow the commentary as it explains each term: kalimat al-baqiyah = word of tawhid, asas = iman, rusukh = heart's certainty, shumukh = ascent of deeds. Note the Hanafi emphasis on inner faith preceding outward action.
These definitions are not merely lexical but legal-theological.
3
Analyze Taftazani's Four-fold Branching
Examine how Taftazani makes four things dependent on the preceding four: kalimah depends on sharia, asas on usul (universal proofs), rusukh on ahkam (rulings), and shumukh on furu' (branches). Understand the logical chain: to accept sharia you need the kalimah; to have firm faith you need strong proofs; to have firm conviction you need strong rulings; to have lofty deeds you need to practice those rulings.
This shows the interdependence of creed and law in Hanafi thought.
4
Synthesize the Overall Message
Conclude that the good tree simile in Hanafi usul demonstrates that when Allah strengthens the principles (through the Book) and elevates the branches (through the address), the believer's faith becomes rooted and deeds ascend. This reinforces the Hanafi method of deriving branches from principles.
The simile is not decorative; it encapsulates a methodological principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتی غایت ونتیجہ ہے ماقبل کیلئے فائدہ : حتی میں تین احتمال ہیں (۱) عاطفہ (۲) ابتدائیہ (۳) جارہ کلمہ باقیہ سے کلمہ توحید مراد ہے اساس سے ایمان اور تصدیق قلبی مراد ہے رسوخ سے اطمینان قلب اور از عان جنان ( دل ) مراد ہے البناء سے عمل صالح مراد ہے جو اقرار کی فرع ہے شموخ سے عمل صالح کا صعود الی محل القبول مراد ہے مقصد عبارت یہ ہوگا کہ جب اللہ تعالی نے کتاب کے ذریعہ سے اصول شریعت ( عقائد یا ادانہ کلیہ ) کو مضبوط کر دیا اور خطاب کے ذریعہ سے ملت حنفیہ کے فروع (اعمال یا احکام) کو بلند کر دیا تو نتیجہ یہ مرتب ہوا کہ کلمہ باقیہ (کلمہ توحید ) کی بنیاد ( ایمان ) مضبوط ہوگئی ۔ اور اسکی عمارت وبناء بلند ہوگئی اور اس کلمہ توحید کی مثال ایسے ہوگئی جیسے شجرہ طیبہ ہے کجھور ) جس کی جڑ تو زمین کے اندر ثابت ہوتی ہے اور اس کی شاخیں آسمان میں ہوتی ہیں اسی طرح کلمہ توحید کی جڑ بھی مضبوط ہوگئی اور شاخیں (اعمال صالحہ ) بلندی کو چھونے لگے۔ فائدہ اولی: حتی اضحت کلمتہ الباقیہ راستہ الاساس شامتہ البناء۔ اس جملہ میں حتی نتیجہ ہے علامہ تفتازانی نے حار چیزوں کو مترتب و متفرع کیا ہے پہلے چار چیزوں پر وہ چار چیزیں یہ ہیں کلمہ۔ اساس۔ رسوخ - شموخ موقوف علیہ چار چیزیں یہ ہیں (۱) شریعت - اصول۔ احکام - فروع کلمہ توحید کو متفرع کیا ہے شریعت پر کہ شریعت وہ کلمہ لا الہ الا اللہ ہے کیونکہ شریعت پر آنے کیلئے کلمہ پڑھنا ضروری ہے اساس کو متفرع و مترتب کیا اصول پر کوہ اسطرح کہ اصول سے مراد دلائل کلیہ ہیں اور اساس سے مراد یمان ہے تو دلائل کلیہ کو دیکھ کر اور مان کر ہی ایمان نصیب ہوتا ہے تو مناسب ہے کہ ایمان کو دلائل پر متفرع کیا جائے۔ رسوخ کو متفرع کیا احکام پر وہ اس طرح کہ علامہ نے کہا کہ اللہ پاک نے شریعت کے دلائل کو پختہ و محکم کیا تو جتنے دلائل پختہ ہونگے اتنا ہی ایمان پختہ ہوگا تو مناسب ہے کہ احکام پر رسوخ کو متفرع کیا جائے ۔ شموخ کو متفرع کیا فروع پر وہ اس طرح کہ فروع سے مراد احکام ہیں تو احکام کو دیکھ کر اور مان کر اعمال صالحہ میں پختگی آئیگی تو خلاصہ یہ کہ علامہ تفتازانی نے حتی کے بعد والے جملے میں چار چیزوں کو متفرع کیا ہے جملہ سابقہ کی چار چیزوں پر
Until (hatta) it is the end and result for the preceding. Benefit: In 'hatta' there are three probabilities: (1) conjunctive (2) inceptive (3) particle of the genitive. By 'remaining word' (kalimat al-baqiyah) is meant the word of tawhid. By 'foundation' (asas) is meant faith and heart's affirmation. By 'firmness' (rusukh) is meant heart's tranquility and certainty. By 'building' (bina') is meant righteous deed, which is a branch of affirmation. By 'loftiness' (shumukh) is meant the ascent of the righteous deed to the place of acceptance. The meaning of the expression would be: When Allah strengthened the principles of the sharia (beliefs or universal proofs) through the book, and elevated the branches of the Hanafi nation (deeds or rulings) through the address, the result was that the foundation (faith) of the remaining word (the word of tawhid) became strong, and its building and construction became high. And the example of this word of tawhid became like a good tree (a date palm) whose root is firm in the ground and its branches are in the sky. Similarly, the root of the word of tawhid became strong and its branches (righteous deeds) began to touch the height. First benefit: 'Hatta adhat kalimat al-baqiyah ra'isat al-asas shamat al-bina'. In this sentence, 'hatta' indicates result. Allama Taftazani made four things dependent and branched from the preceding four things. The four things are: kalimah, asas, rusukh, shumukh. The depended-upon four things are: (1) sharia (2) usul (3) ahkam (4) furu'. The word of tawhid is made a branch of sharia, because to come to sharia, reciting the kalimah is necessary. Asas is made dependent on usul, because usul means universal proofs, and asas means faith. Through seeing and believing the universal proofs, faith is attained. So it is appropriate to make faith a branch of proofs. Rusukh is made dependent on ahkam, because Allah made the proofs of sharia firm and strong; as the proofs become stronger, faith becomes stronger. So it is appropriate to make rusukh a branch of ahkam. Shumukh is made dependent on furu', because furu' means rulings. By seeing and believing the rulings, righteous deeds become firm. The summary is that Allama Taftazani branched four things from the four things of the preceding sentence in the sentence after 'hatta'.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the Quranic simile of the good tree (shajarah tayyibah) as applied to the relationship between foundational principles and derived branches. The commentator first explains the word 'hatta' (until/so that) which introduces the result. Then he unpacks the terms: 'remaining word' means the kalimah of tawhid, 'foundation' is faith, 'firmness' is heart's certainty, 'building' is righteous deeds, and 'loftiness' is the acceptance of deeds. The overall meaning is that when Allah strengthens the principles (either beliefs or universal proofs) through the Qur'an, and elevates the branches (either deeds or rulings) through His address, the result is that the foundation of tawhid becomes strong and its branches ascend. The simile of the date palm illustrates this: its root is firm in the ground and its branches reach the sky. Then, the first benefit (fa'idah ula) from Allama Taftazani is that he makes a four-fold branching: kalimah from sharia, asas from usul, rusukh from ahkam, and shumukh from furu'. This establishes a systematic dependency showing that the strength of faith (asas) depends on the clarity of proofs (usul), the firmness of faith (rusukh) depends on the strength of rulings (ahkam), and the loftiness of deeds (shumukh) depends on the practice of rulings (furu'). This is a typical Hanafi method of showing interconnections between usul and furu' in both creed and law.

Key Terms
کلمہ باقیہ (kalimat al-baqiyah): The remaining word; in this context, the word of tawhid (la ilaha illa Allah).
اساس (asas): Foundation; here it refers to faith (iman) which is the basis.
رسوخ (rusukh): Firmness; here it means the heart's tranquility and certainty in faith.
شموخ (shumukh): Loftiness; here it means the ascent of righteous deeds to the place of acceptance.
شجرہ طیبہ (shajarah tayyibah): Good tree; the date palm, used as a simile for the word of tawhid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sharia
B) Usul (universal proofs)
C) Ahkam (rulings)
D) Furu' (branches)

Key Takeaway
The good tree simile in Hanafi usul establishes a systematic dependency: strong principles (usul) yield strong branches (furu'), both in creed and law.

Three Interpretations of 'أولاً وثانياً' in Praise of Allah
Explaining three possible meanings of 'أولاً وثانياً' in the author's phrase detailing الحمد

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between three interpretations of a concise textual phrase and apply this expansion technique to other usul texts.

Core Idea
A single phrase can yield multiple valid meanings—scripture and reason illuminate each dimension.

The author’s concise expression 'أولاً وثانياً' in praising Allah opens a window into how classical scholars expand brief statements. This lesson shows three distinct ways the commentator unpacks that phrase, each grounded in Quranic proof and theological reasoning. Understanding this method is essential for interpreting dense texts in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Phrase
Locate the exact expression 'أولاً وثانياً' in the source passage. It is part of the author's description of الحمد (praise). This phrase is the anchor for the entire expansion.
2
List the Three Interpretations
Read through the three interpretations (وجوه) proposed by the commentator. For each, note the basis: 1) essence vs. blessings, 2) creation vs. perpetuation with surah examples, 3) this world vs. Hereafter with Quranic verses.
Each interpretation is a distinct way to categorize types of praise.
3
Examine the Scriptural Proofs
Identify the Quranic references used to support each interpretation: Surah al-Fatihah (all), al-An'am (creation), al-Kahf (perpetuation), Saba (creation2), al-Mala'ikah (perpetuation2), and the verses 'وله الحمد في الأولى والآخرة' and 'آخر دعواهم أن الحمد لله رب العالمين'.
4
Analyze the Commentator's Method
Observe how the commentator moves from the author's concise phrase to multiple possible meanings. This is 'expansion' (تفصيل) – a key skill in usul al-fiqh for interpreting mujmal (ambiguous) texts.
The commentator does not pick one; he presents all probabilities.
5
Apply to a Fiqh Example
Think of a concise fiqh ruling, e.g., 'الطهور شطر الإيمان' (Purity is half of faith). How might a commentator expand 'طهور' and 'إيمان'? This mirrors the method used here.
This step builds transferable skill.

And as for the detail of praise by his saying 'firstly and secondly', it admits several interpretations. The first: praise can be for blessing and other than it. So Allah is deserving of praise firstly for the perfection of His essence and the greatness of His attributes, and secondly for the beauty of His blessings and the abundance of His favors, among which is the success to compose this book. The second: that the blessings of Allah despite their multitude reduce to creation and sustenance firstly, and to creation and perpetuation secondly. So he praises Him for the two categories, following the surahs opened with 'al-hamdu lillah' where in al-Fatihah reference is made to all, in al-An'am to creation, in al-Kahf to perpetuation firstly, in Saba to creation, and in al-Mala'ikah (Fatir) to perpetuation secondly. The third: consideration of His saying 'and to Him is praise in the first and the last' meaning that He deserves praise in this world for what is known by argument of His perfection and reaches the servants from His bounty, and in the Hereafter for what will be witnessed of His majesty and beheld of His blessings that no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to any human heart. And to that points His saying 'and the end of their call is that praise is for Allah, Lord of the worlds'. Translation: And as for the detail of praise by the author's saying 'firstly and secondly', it admits several interpretations. Reason (1): Praise can be for blessing and other than it. So Allah is deserving of praise firstly for the perfection of His essence and the greatness of His attributes, and secondly for the beauty of His blessings and the abundance of His favors, among which is the success to compose this book. Reason (2): The blessings of Allah despite their multitude reduce to creation and sustenance firstly, and to creation and perpetuation secondly. So the author praises Allah for the two categories, following the surahs opened with 'al-hamdu lillah' such that in al-Fatihah reference is made to all, in al-An'am to creation firstly, in al-Kahf to perpetuation firstly, in Saba to creation secondly, and in al-Mala'ikah (Fatir) to perpetuation secondly. Reason (3): Consideration of His saying 'and to Him is praise in the first and the last' meaning that He deserves praise in this world for what is known by argument of His perfection and reaches the servants from His bounty, and in the Hereafter for what will be witnessed of His majesty and beheld of His blessings that no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to any human heart. And to that points His saying 'and the end of their call is that praise is for Allah, Lord of the worlds'. Answer to an implied question: The question arises: what is meant by the author's saying 'firstly and secondly'? Answer: There are multiple probabilities.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the author's phrase 'أولاً وثانياً' (firstly and secondly) used in detailing the praise of Allah. The commentator presents three possible interpretations. The first interpretation divides praise between that which is due to Allah's inherent perfection (firstly) and that which is due to His blessings (secondly). The second interpretation relates to the types of divine acts: creation and sustenance (إيجاد وإبقاء) as two categories, with examples from various surahs that begin with 'الحمد لله'. The third interpretation connects the phrase to the Quranic verse 'وله الحمد في الأولى والآخرة' and explains that praise in this world is based on intellectual argument for His perfection, while in the Hereafter it is based on direct witnessing of His majesty and blessings. This demonstrates how the commentator uses Quranic intertextuality and thematic analysis to elucidate the author's concise expression.

Key Terms
إيجاد (iijaad): The act of bringing into existence, creation.
إبقاء (ibqaa): The act of preserving in existence, sustenance.
تفصيل (tafseel): Detail or elaboration; here meaning providing a detailed explanation of the author's concise statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Blessings for the good and punishment for the evil.
B) Creation (إيجاد) and perpetuation (إبقاء).
C) Worldly blessings and religious blessings.
D) Praise for attributes and praise for actions.

Key Takeaway
A single concise phrase like 'أولاً وثانياً' can be expanded into multiple valid scriptural interpretations, demonstrating the usul al-fiqh skill of تَفْصِيل (elaboration).

Critique of Taftazani on the Basmalah
Critique of Taftazani's argument against basmalah being part of Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate two objections raised against Taftazani's view that the basmalah is not part of the Quran, using the concepts of textual consistency and practical consensus (ijma' amali).

Core Idea
Taftazani's dismissal of basmalah as part of the Quran contradicts both textual harmony and the universal practice of Muslim authors.

This passage critiques the view of Taftazani regarding the status of the basmalah (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim). The commentator presents two arguments: first, an inconsistency in treating basmalah differently from other Quranic verses like "To Him ascends the good word," and second, a practical consensus (ijma' amali) demonstrated by the universal practice of authors including basmalah while often omitting praise. This lesson will guide you through these objections and their implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim Being Critiqued
Taftazani argued that the basmalah is written only for blessing (tabarruk), not as a valid part of the Quran. This is the target of the critique.
2
Analyze the First Objection: Textual Inconsistency
If basmalah is not part of the Quran, but the verse 'To Him ascends the good word' (which includes hamd) is part, it creates an inequality. However, the author (Sadr al-Shariah) was striving to equate basmalah and hamd, so Taftazani's view contradicts that effort.
This objection highlights internal inconsistency.
3
Analyze the Second Objection: Practical Consensus (Ijma' Amali)
There is a practical consensus that starting with basmalah is necessary in every matter, whereas mentioning hamd is not. Countless authors include basmalah but omit hamd, proving basmalah's unique status. Taftazani's response contradicts this consensus.
Ijma' amali is a valid source of evidence in Hanafi usul.
4
Evaluate the Force of the Critique
The critique uses two strong arguments: textual harmony and consensus. In Hanafi usul, consensus is a binding proof. Therefore, Taftazani's view is deemed inconsistent and against the established practice.
The critique does not provide a direct counter-argument; it exposes flaws.

He wrote the basmalah, but only for blessing, not for the purpose of being a valid part. So in all three cases, the hadith was acted upon and the implicit reference before the mentioned one was not necessary. Commentary: The response of Sharh Taftazani is open to objection for multiple reasons. (1) It appears from this that the basmalah is not part of the book, while 'To Him ascends the good word' from the praises (i.e., hamd) is part of the book. This creates inequality between them, whereas the author was striving hard to equate them as mentioned earlier. So the sharh's statement contradicts the previous. (2) There is consensus that starting with the basmalah is necessary in every matter, while mentioning hamd is not necessary. This is practical consensus. That is why many authors have omitted hamd, like the author of al-Kafiya and al-Bukhari, but no one has omitted the basmalah. So the sharh's response also contradicts consensus.

Commentary
This passage is a critical response to Taftazani's view on the basmalah. The commentator presents two objections: first, if basmalah is not part of the Quran but the verse 'To Him ascends the good word' (which includes praise) is part of it, there is inconsistency, especially since Sadr al-Shariah was trying to show parallel importance. Second, the practical consensus of Muslim authors shows that basmalah is universally included while praise is often omitted, proving basmalah's essential status. This refutes Taftazani's argument.

Key Takeaway

Metaphorical Interpretation of 'Su'ud' and Derivation of 'Kalim'
Explaining metaphor and grammatical derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of isti'arah to interpret 'su'ud' metaphorically and analyze the three meanings of 'min' to understand the relationship between 'kalim' and 'kalimah'.

Core Idea
'Su'ud' is metaphorical for spiritual rank; 'kalim' relates to 'kalimah' through multiple grammatical readings of 'min'.

This passage tackles a theological objection to the literal meaning of 'ascending' in the Quranic verse about good words ascending to Allah. The author resolves it by invoking isti'arah (metaphor) and then explores three linguistic interpretations of the preposition 'min' in the phrase 'al-kalim min al-kalimah'. This analysis demonstrates how precise linguistic tools are essential in usul al-fiqh for deriving sound meanings from sacred texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the literal meaning of su'ud
Examine the lexical definition: su'ud means movement from a lower place to a higher place.
This is the haqiqah (literal) meaning.
2
Recognize the theological objection
If taken literally, the verse would imply that Allah is in a physical direction, which contradicts His transcendence.
The objection is based on the impossibility of direction for Allah.
3
Apply the metaphorical interpretation
Understand that su'ud is used as isti'arah: it means spiritual direction towards high rank, not physical movement.
The qarinah (indicator) is Allah's transcendence, which shifts the meaning from haqiqah to majaz.
4
Analyze the three meanings of 'min'
For each interpretation of the preposition, derive how 'kalim' relates to 'kalimah': (1) min as locative means kalim is derived from kalimah; (2) min as conjunctive means a connection like tamr to tamrah; (3) min as consideration means kalim is considered in terms of kalimah.
Each interpretation is linguistically valid and shows the richness of Arabic.
5
Synthesize the benefit
Recognize that multiple valid readings can coexist, and that metaphorical interpretation is necessary to maintain theological correctness.
This approach is a hallmark of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

And ascending is the movement, etc. Purpose: Explanation of the lexical meaning of su'ud and the response to the objection. The lexical meaning of su'ud is movement from a lower place to a higher place. Objection: This meaning cannot be realized here because the meaning would be 'they ascend to Allah', implying Allah is in a place, which is impossible as He is free from place and direction. Answer: They respond using metaphor: here su'ud has a metaphorical meaning, i.e., 'directing towards the one who is high in station and rank'. That is, the good words are directed towards Allah, who is high in rank, not in place or direction. And the phrase 'al-kalim min al-kalimah is like al-tamr min al-tamrah'. Benefit: There can be multiple interpretations of 'min' in al-kalim min al-kalimah: (1) min is a locative adverb, meaning that kalim is derived from kalimah. (2) min is conjunctive, meaning the connection of kalim to kalimah is like the connection of tamr to tamrah. (3) min is in the sense of consideration, meaning kalim in consideration of kalimah is like tamr in consideration of tamrah.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This section addresses the theological objection to the literal meaning of 'ascending' in the Quranic verse. The author explains that 'su'ud' is used metaphorically to refer to spiritual elevation towards Allah's rank, not physical direction. Then he examines the phrase 'al-kalim min al-kalimah' and provides three grammatical interpretations of the preposition 'min', showing the linguistic richness of the text and how 'kalim' relates to 'kalimah' as a generic noun to its singular.

Key Terms
صعود (su'ud): Lexical meaning: physical ascending; here metaphorical: spiritual direction towards high rank
استعارہ (isti'arah): Metaphorical usage, shifting from literal to figurative meaning
من (min): Preposition with multiple functions: locative (derivation), conjunctive (connection), and consideration (perspective)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul employs metaphor (isti'arah) to reconcile linguistic appearance with theological principles, and a single phrase can have multiple valid grammatical interpretations.

Explanation of 'Min Mahamid al-Kalim' and Acceptance of Deeds
Explaining the phrase and the hadith on acceptance with deeds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the linguistic features of 'mahamid al-kalim', distinguish between hamd and shukr, and explain the conditionality of acceptance of good words upon righteous deeds using the good tree metaphor.

Core Idea
Words of praise are only accepted when rooted in belief and accompanied by righteous deeds.

This passage from Misk al-Malih provides a layered commentary on the phrase 'min mahamid al-kalim' from al-Tawdih. The commentator dissects the grammar, clarifies the distinction between hamd and shukr, cites a hadith linking acceptance to righteous deeds, and uses the Quranic good tree metaphor to show that belief is the root and action the fruit. This lesson guides you through the textual analysis and the derived usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Parse the grammatical status of 'kalim' and 'mahamid'
Identify that 'kalim' is a conceptual plural and 'mahamid' is an indefinite plural used for generality. Note how the indefinite noun with description can indicate generality.
This is a Hanafi application of the principle 'al-nakirah ta'mmu bi al-wasf'.
2
Distinguish between 'hamd' and 'shukr'
Define hamd as praise by the tongue, and shukr as gratitude by tongue, action, or belief. This distinction is essential for understanding the scope of 'mahamid al-kalim'.
The Hanafi school emphasizes that hamd is specifically verbal.
3
Analyze the hadith on acceptance
The hadith states that the words Subhan Allah, etc., are brought by an angel to Allah's presence, but they are not accepted if the speaker has no righteous deed. This makes righteous deeds a condition (shart) for acceptance.
The hadith is ahad, so it is zanni in both transmission and meaning, but it is authoritative in Hanafi usul.
4
Interpret the good tree metaphor
The commentator likens hamd to a good tree: belief is the root, and righteous deeds are the branches. Quoting Quran 14:24, he shows that without belief, hamd is uprooted; without deeds, it bears no fruit.
This metaphor links the linguistic analysis to the broader usul principle that acceptance of worship depends on both inner conviction and outward action.

Source Text

مسک الملیح شرح التوضيح والتلويح
عبارت اسطرح ہوگی ۔ والكلم ان كان جمعا فهو جمع يفرق بينه وبين واحده بالتاء وكل جمع يفرق الخ مقصود مصنف یہ ہے کلم اگر جمع ہے تو یہ جمع معنوی ہے لفظ مفرد ہے معنی جنسی کے اعتبار سے جمع ہے اور ہر ایسی جمع کی صفت مذکر بھی لائی جاسکتی ہے مونث بھی تو اس معنی میں نہ تو کوئی شک ہے اور نہ ہی خزازہ ہے (۳) مصنف نے ان شرطیہ کا ذکر با طب را از طب البتہ ہم کیا ہے کیونکہ بعض آئمہ اس کی جمعیت کے قائل نہیں ہیں اسی بناء پر مخاطب کو جمعیت میں شک ہو گیا۔ قوله من محامد من الكلم بيانا لهعلى ماقال النبي عليه السلام هو سبحان الله والحمد لله ولا اله الا لله والله اكبر اذا قالها العبد عرج بها الملك الى السماء فحيا بها وجه الرحمن فا ذالم يكن له عمل صالح لم يقبل وانما صلح الجمع المنكر بيانا للمعرف المستغرق لما سيجئ من ان النكرة تعم بالوصف كامرأة كوفية ولان التنكير هنا للتكثير و هو ينا سب التعميم والمحامد جمع محمدة بمعنى الحمد وهم مقابلة الجميل من نعمة وغيرها بالثناء والتعظيم باللسان والشكر مقابلة النعمة باظهار تعظيم المنعم قولا او عملاً او اعتقاد افلا ختصاص الحمد باللسان كان بيان الكلم بها انسب والمشارع جمع مشرعة الماء وهى مورد الشاربة والشرع والشريعة ما شرع الله لعباده من الدين اى اظهر و بين وحاصله الطريقة المعهودة الثابتة من النبي عليه السلام جعلها على طريقة الاستعاره المكنية بمنزلة روضات و جناتٍ فاثبت لها مشارع يردها المتعطشون الى زلال الرحمة والرضوان وبهذا الطريق اثبت لقبول العبادة الذى هو مهب الطاف الرحمن و مطلع انوار الغفران ريح الصبا التني بها روح الابدان ونماء الاغصان فان القبول الاول ريح الصباء ومهبها المستوى مطلع الشمس اذا استوى الليل والنهار ويقابلها الدبور والعرب تزعم ان الدبور تزعج السحاب وتشخصه في الهواء ثم تسوقه فاذ علا كشفت عنه واستقبلته الصبا فوزعت بعضه على بعض حتى يصير كسفا واحد اثم ينزل مطر اینمی به الاشجار والقبول الثانى من المصادر الشاذة لم يسمع له ثان والنماء الزيادة والارتفاع يقال نمى ينمى نماء ونما ينمونموا وحقيقة النمو الزيادة والارتفاع في اقطار الجسم على تناسب طبيعى ثم فى وصف المحامد بما ذكر تلميح الى قوله تعالى ضرب الله مثلا كلمة طيبة كشجرة طيبة اصلها ثابت وفرعها في السماء فان المحامد لما كانت هي الكلم الطيب والكلمة الطيبة كشجرة طيبة فالمحمدة شجر لها اصل هو الايمان والاعتقاد أن وفرع هو الاعمال والطاعات
ہے اس سے قبل واؤ محذوف ہے (۲) اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے ان شرطیہ ہے تو پھر یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ یہاں جزاء محذوف

شرح التوضيح والتلويح
وتحقيق ذلك ان الحمد وان كان فى اللغة فعل اللسان خاصة الا ان حمد الله تعالى على ما صرح به الامام الرازي رحمه الله تعالى فى تفسيره ليس قول القائل احمد الله بل ما يشعر بتعظيمه وينبى عن تمجيده من اعتقاد اتصافه بصفات الكمال والترجمة عن ذلك بالمقال والاتيان بما يدل عليه من الاعمال فالاعتقاد اصل لولاه لكان الحمد كشجرة خبيثة اجتثت من فوق الأرض مالها من قرارو العمل فرع الولاه لما كان للحمد نماء إلى الله تعالى وقبول عنده بمنزلة دوحة لا غصن لها وشجرة لا ثمرة عليها اذ العمل هو الوسيلة إلى نيل الجنات ورفع الدرجات قال الله تعالى والعمل الصالح يرفعه وفي الحديث فاذالم يكن له عمل صالح لم يقبل فاشار المصنف الى ان لشجرة المحامد اصلاً ثابتاً هو الاعتقاد الراسخ الاسلامى الميتنى على علم التوحيد والصفات و فرعانا ميا الى الله تعالى مقبولا عنده هو العمل الصالح الموافق للشريعة المطهرة المبتنى على علم الشرائع والا حكام واشار الى لاختصاص والدوام بقوله اليه يصعد الكلم بتقديم الظرف المفيد للاختصاص و لفظ المضارع المنبىء عن الاستمرار .
ترجمہ ! من محامد الکلم سے حال ہے اور اس کیلئے بیان ہے جیسا کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے فرمایا کہ وہ کلم الطیب سبحان اللہ والحمد للہ الہ الاللہ واللہ اکبر ہیں جب ان کلمات کو بندہ کہتا ہے تو فرشتہ ان کو لے کر آسمان کی طرف چڑھ جاتا ہے پس ان کلمات کے ساتھ رحمن کی ذات کو تحفہ پیش کرتا ہے پس جب اس بندے کیلئے اور نیک عمل نہو تو یہ کلمات قبول نہیں کیے جاتے ۔ اور سوائے اس کے نہیں جمع منکر صلاحیت رکھتی ہے بیان بنے گی جمع معرف متفرق کیلئے جیسا کہ عنقریب آجائیگا کہ نکرہ عام ہو جاتا ہے صفت کیساتھ جیسا کہ امرءۃ کوفیہ اور اس لیے کہ تنکیر یہاں تکثیر کے لئے ہے اور وہ مناسب ہے تمیم کے۔ اور محامد محمدۃ کی جمع ہے بمعنی الحمد ہے اور وہ مقابلہ ہے اچھے کام کا نعمت سے ہو یا غیر نعمت سے ثناء اور تعظیم کے ساتھ زبان کے ساتھ اور شکر نعمت کا مقابلہ کرنا ہے منعم کی تعظیم کے اظہار کے ساتھ قول یا عمل یا اعتقاد کیساتھ ۔ پس حمد کے اختصاص باللسان کیوجہ سے محامد کے ساتھ کلم کا بیان زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ اور مشارع مشرعہ کی جمع ہے اور وہ پانی پینے والوں کے وارد ہونے کی جگہ ہے ( گھاٹ ) اور شرع اور شریعت وہ ہے جسکو اللہ تعالیٰ اپنے بندوں کیلئے ظاہر کرے دین سے۔ ای اظہر دبین سے شرع کا معنی بیان کیا ( یعنی ظاہر اور بیان کر دے) اور انکا حاصل یہ ہے کہ وہ طریقہ جو معلوم اور ثابت ہے نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام سے ۔ مصنف نے بنایا شریعت کو استعارہ مکنیہ کے طریقہ پر بمنزلہ باغات و جنات کے پھر ثابت کیا ان کیلئے مشارع کو جن پر وارد ہوتے ہیں رحمت اور رضوان کے خالص پانی کے پیاسے لوگ اور اسی طریقہ کے ساتھ ثابت کیا قبولیت عبادت کیلئے جو کہ رحمن کے الطاف کی
And the word if it is plural, it is a plural that is distinguished from its singular by the ta' and every plural... The author's intent is that if 'kalim' is plural, it is a conceptual plural; the word is singular, but in terms of generic meaning it is plural, and for every such plural, the adjective can be masculine or feminine, so in that meaning there is no doubt and no ambiguity. The author mentioned the conditional 'in' with 'balā' [؟] because some imams do not accept its plural form; based on this, the addressee doubts its plurality. His statement 'min mahamid al-kalim' is a circumstantial clause and an explanation for what the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar.' When the servant says them, an angel ascends with them to the sky and greets the face of the Most Merciful with them. If the servant has no righteous deed, they are not accepted. And the indefinite plural is only suitable as an explanation for the definite comprehensive [noun] because, as will come, the indefinite is general due to description, like 'imra'ah kufiyyah', and because the tanween here indicates multiplication, which is suitable for generalization. And 'mahamid' is the plural of 'mahmadah' meaning 'hamd', and it is the counterpart of a good deed, whether from a blessing or otherwise, with praise and glorification by the tongue. And 'shukr' is the counterpart of a blessing by showing glorification of the Bestower, verbally, by action, or by belief. Since 'hamd' is specific to the tongue, explaining 'kalim' with it is more appropriate. And 'mashari'' is the plural of 'mashra'ah' meaning a watering place. And 'shar'' and 'shari'ah' is what Allah has legislated for His servants from the religion, i.e., He made it apparent and clear. Its summary is the established customary way from the Prophet, peace be upon him. The author made it, by way of metaphorical analogy, like gardens and orchards, then established for them watering places that the thirsty for the pure water of mercy and pleasure seek. And by this way, he established for the acceptance of worship, which is the blowing of the zephyr of the Merciful's favors and the rising place of the lights of forgiveness, the east wind (sabā) which brings life to bodies and growth to branches. For the first acceptance is the east wind, and its rising is the equinox when day and night are equal, and it is opposite the west wind (dabūr). The Arabs claim that the west wind stirs the clouds and lifts them into the air, then drives them, and when they rise high, it unveils them, and the east wind meets them and distributes them one upon another until they become a single mass, then rain descends by which trees grow. And 'al-qabūl al-thānī' is from rare verbal nouns for which no second is heard. And 'al-namā'' is increase and elevation. It is said 'namā yanmī namā'an' and 'namā yanmū numuwwan'. The reality of growth is increase and elevation in the dimensions of the body in a natural proportion. Then, in describing the 'mahamid' with what was mentioned, there is an allusion to the verse: 'Allah sets forth the parable of a good word as a good tree, its root firmly fixed and its branches in the sky.' Since 'mahamid' are the good words and the good word is like a good tree, so 'mahmadah' is a tree whose root is faith and belief, and its branch is deeds and obedience. Before this, the waw is deleted. If it is conceded that it is conditional 'in', then the answer is that here the answer is omitted. And the verification of that is that 'hamd', although in language it is an act specific to the tongue, but praising Allah Almighty, as stated by Imam al-Razi in his exegesis, is not the saying of the speaker 'I praise Allah', but rather what indicates His glorification and signifies His exaltation from belief in His attributes of perfection, and expressing that by speech and performing what indicates it from actions. So belief is the root; without it, 'hamd' would be like a bad tree uprooted from above the ground having no stability. And action is the branch; without it, 'hamd' would have no growth towards Allah and no acceptance with Him; it would be like a tree with no branch and a tree with no fruit. For action is the means to attaining gardens and raising ranks. Allah says: 'And righteous deed raises it.' And in the hadith: 'If he has no righteous deed, it is not accepted.' So the author pointed out that the tree of 'mahamid' has a firm root, which is the firmly rooted Islamic belief based on the science of tawhid and attributes, and a branch rising to Allah and accepted by Him, which is the righteous deed in accordance with the pure Shari'ah based on the science of laws and rulings. And he pointed to specificity and continuity by his saying: 'To Him ascends the good word' with the advance of the adverb indicating specificity and the present tense verb indicating continuity.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'min mahamid al-kalim' (from the praiseworthy words) from the text of al-Tawdih. The commentator begins by clarifying the grammatical status of 'kalim' as a conceptual plural, noting that adjectives can be masculine or feminine for such plurals. He then explains that the indefinite plural 'mahamid' is used as a description for the definite comprehensive term 'al-kalim' to indicate generality and multiplicity, as indefinite nouns can be made general by description. The hadith about the words of praise (Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, etc.) is cited to show that these words are the 'good words' that ascend to Allah, but their acceptance is conditional upon the presence of righteous deeds. Without deeds, they are not accepted. The commentator then provides a detailed linguistic distinction between 'hamd' and 'shukr': hamd is praise by the tongue for any good, while shukr is showing gratitude to the Bestower by any means. He then engages in a metaphorical explanation comparing the Shari'ah to gardens and watering places, and acceptance of worship to the east wind that brings life. He connects this to the Quranic verse of the good tree, interpreting the root as faith and the branches as deeds. The passage emphasizes that hamd without belief and action is incomplete. The commentary is based on the Hanafi usul tradition, drawing on Imam al-Razi's tafsir and the hadith, and uses metaphorical language typical of later Hanafi commentaries.

Key Terms
محامد (mahamid): Plural of mahmadah, meaning acts of praise (hamd)
الحمد (al-hamd): Praise by the tongue for a good deed, whether blessing or not
الشكر (al-shukr): Showing gratitude for a blessing by verbally, action, or belief

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is required for the words of praise (Subhan Allah, etc.) to be accepted?
A) Recitation many times
B) Accompanying righteous deeds
C) Recitation in Arabic only
D) Recitation in congregation

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of verbal praise depends on righteous deeds; belief is the root and action is the fruit.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
6 min
Components of Hamd: Belief, Speech, and Action
Expanding the meaning of hamd to include belief and action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three components of hamd (belief, speech, action) and explain why belief and action are necessary for its acceptance according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
True praise of Allah requires belief as the root and righteous action as the branch; words alone are not sufficient.

The source passage from the sharh of Al-Tawdih unpacks the comprehensive meaning of hamd (praise) as understood in the Hanafi tradition. It goes beyond the simple linguistic definition—speech of the tongue—to include the essential dimensions of belief and action. Using the powerful metaphors of a tree, the author shows that praise without belief is rootless and praise without action is fruitless. This lesson will guide you through the textual analysis and help you internalize the usul principle that acceptance of worship depends on the integration of inner conviction and outward deeds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic vs. shar'i meaning of hamd
The passage begins by acknowledging that linguistically, hamd is an act of the tongue. However, the shar'i meaning, as stated by Imam al-Razi, is broader: it includes belief (i'tiqad), speech (qawl), and action ('amal). Identify this distinction in the text.
Notice the phrase 'ليس قول القائل احمد الله بل ما يشعر بتعظيمه وينبى عن تمجيده' – it's not just saying 'I praise Allah' but that which conveys glorification.
2
Locate the three components and the tree metaphor
Find where the text explicitly states that hamd consists of belief, speech, and action. Then note how the tree metaphor assigns belief as the root and action as the branch. The author contrasts this with an evil tree (belief absent) and a branchless tree (action absent).
The metaphor is developed using Quranic imagery: 'like an evil tree uprooted from above the earth' and 'like a tree without a branch and without fruit'.
3
Analyse the Quranic evidence and hadith
The passage cites Quran 35:10: 'To Him ascends the good word, and righteous action raises it.' Also a hadith: 'When there is no righteous action, it is not accepted.' Identify how these texts establish the necessity of action alongside verbal praise.
The author highlights the prefixed adverb (إليه) indicating exclusivity, and the present tense (يصعد) indicating continuity, to reinforce that only praise accompanied by action rises continuously.
4
Derive the usul principle
From the analysis, draw the principle that hamd (and by extension any act of worship) requires both correct belief and righteous action for acceptance. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul for evaluating the validity of deeds.
This principle is not about the fiqh ruling of hamd being wajib or mandub, but about the condition for its reward and acceptance.

ترجمہ ! من محامد الکلم سے حال ہے اور اس کیلئے بیان ہے جیسا کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے فرمایا کہ وہ کلم الطیب سبحان اللہ والحمد للہ الہ الاللہ واللہ اکبر ہیں جب ان کلمات کو بندہ کہتا ہے تو فرشتہ ان کو لے کر آسمان کی طرف چڑھ جاتا ہے پس ان کلمات کے ساتھ رحمن کی ذات کو تحفہ پیش کرتا ہے پس جب اس بندے کیلئے اور نیک عمل نہ ہو تو یہ کلمات قبول نہیں کیے جاتے ۔ اور سوائے اس کے نہیں جمع منکر صلاحیت رکھتی ہے بیان بنے گی جمع معرف متفرق کیلئے جیسا کہ عنقریب آجائیگا کہ نکرہ عام ہو جاتا ہے صفت کیسا تھ جیسا کہ امرءۃ کوفیہ اور اس لیے کہ تنکیر یہاں تکثیر کے لئے ہے اور وہ مناسب ہے تمیم کے۔ اور محامد محمدۃ کی جمع ہے بمعنی الحمد ہے اور وہ مقابلہ ہے اچھے کام کا نعمت سے ہو یا غیر نعمت سے ثناء اور تعظیم کے ساتھ زبان کے ساتھ اور شکر نعمت کا مقابلہ کرنا ہے منعم کی تعظیم کے اظہار کے ساتھ قول یا عمل یا اعتقاد کیساتھ ۔ پس حمد کے اختصاص باللسان کیوجہ سے محامد کے ساتھ کلم کا بیان زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ اور مشارع مشرعہ کی جمع ہے اور وہ پانی پینے والوں کے وارد ہونے کی جگہ ہے ( گھاٹ ) اور شرع اور شریعت وہ ہے جسکو اللہ تعالیٰ اپنے بندوں کیلئے ظاہر کرے دین سے۔ ای اظہر دبین سے شرع کا معنی بیان کیا ( یعنی ظاہر اور بیان کر دے) اور انکا حاصل یہ ہے کہ وہ طریقہ جو معلوم اور ثابت ہے نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام سے ۔ مصنف نے بنایا شریعت کو استعارہ مکنیہ کے طریقہ پر بمنزلہ باغات و جنات کے پھر ثابت کیا ان کیلئے مشارع کو جن پر وارد ہوتے ہیں رحمت اور رضوان کے خالص پانی کے پیاسے لوگ اور اسی طریقہ کے ساتھ ثابت کیا قبولیت عبادت کیلئے جو کہ رحمن کے الطاف کی
هواؤں کا چلنا ہے اور غفران کے انوار کا طلوع ہونا ہے ( ثابت کیا ) باد صباء کو جسکے ساتھ بدن besturant
ہے کیونکہ قبول اول کا معنی بادصباء ہے اور اسکا برابر چلنا سورج کے طلوع ہونے کی جگہ ہے جبکہ دن رات برابر ہوں اور اس کے
مقابلہ میں دبور آتی ہے اور عرب گمان کرتے ہیں کہ دبور ہوا بادلوں کو اکھیڑ تی ہے اور ان کو بلند کرتی ہے ہوا میں پھر چلاتی ہے ان بادلوں کو پس جب وہ بادل بلند ہو جاتے ہیں تو یہ ہوا اس سے ہٹ جاتی ہے اور باصباء اسکا استقبال کرتی ہے اور اس کے بعض کو بعض پر تہ بتہ رکھ دیتی ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ ایک ٹکڑا بن جاتا ہے پھر وہ بارش برساتی ہے جس سے درمخت بڑھتے ہیں اور قبول ثانی مصادر شازہ میں سے ہے اس کیلئے کوئی دوسرا لفظ نہیں سنا گیا۔ اور نماء زیادتی اور ارتفاع کو کہتے ہیں کہا جاتا ہے نمی ینمی نماء ( ازض) اور نما نمونموا ( از ن) اور نمو کا حقیقی معنی ہے زیادتی جسم کے تمام اطراف میں تناسب طبیعی کے طریقے پر پھر محامد کو موصوف کرنے میں اس صفت کے ساتھ جو ذکر کی گئی ہے اشارہ ہے اللہ تعالٰی کے قول وضرب اللہ مثلا کلمہ طيبة كشجرۃ طبیة اصلها ثابت وفرعهافی السماد کی طرف پس بیشک محامد جب تھے وہی کلمات طیبہ اور کلمہ طیبہ بمنزلہ شجرہ طیبہ کے ہے پس محمد ہ ایک درخت ہے جس کیلئے جڑ ہے وہ ایمان اور اعتقادات ہیں اور شاخ ہے وہ اعمال اور طاعات ہیں۔ اور اسکی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ حمد اگر چہ لغت میں زبان کا فعل ہے خاصکر مگر تحقیق اللہ تعالیٰ کی حمد جیسا کہ امام رازی نے تصریح کی ہے اسکی تفسیر میں نہیں ہے قائل کا قول الحمد اللہ بلکہ حمد وہ ہے جو شعر ہو اسکی تعظیم کے ساتھ اور خبر دے اسکی بزرگی بیان کرنے سے یعنی اعتقاد رکھنا اس کے متصف ہونے کا صفات کمال کے ساتھ اور ترجمانی کرنا اسکی زبان سے کہنے کیسا تھ اور لے آنا اس چیز کو جو دلالت کرے اس پر اعمال سے پس اعتقاد اصل اور جڑ ہے اگر وہ نہ ہو تو حمد شجرہ خبیثہ کی طرح ہوگی جوا کھیر دیا گیا ہوز مین کے اوپر اس کو کوئی قرار نہ ہو اور عمل فرع اور شاخ ہے اگر وہ نہ ہو تو حمد کے لئے اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف نما نہیں ہوگا اور اس ہاں قبولیت نہیں ہوگی بمنزلہ تنہ کے جسکی شاخ نہ ہو اور بمنزلہ درخت کے جس پر کوئی پھل نہ ہو اس لئے کہ عمل وہی وسیلہ ہے جنات کو حاصل کرنے کا اور درجات کو بلند کرنے کا اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا العمل الصالح يرفعہ اور حدیث پاک میں ارشاد ہے کہ جب اس کیلئے عمل صالح نہ ہو تو وہ مقبول نہیں ہوگا پس اشارہ کیا مصنف نے اس بات کی طرف کہ محامد کے درخت کیلئے ایک اصل ثابت ہے وہ اعتقاد وراسخ ہے اسلامی جو کہ بنی ہے علم تو حید وصفات پر اور ایک شاخ و فرع ہے جو بڑھنے والی ہے اللہ تعالی کی طرف مقبول ہے اس کے ہاں اور وہ عمل صالح ہے جو موافق ہو شریعت مطہرہ کے جو معنی ہو علم الشرائع والا حکام پر اور اشارہ کیا مصنف نے اختصاص اور دوام کی طرف الیہ مصعد الكلم الطيب کیسا تھ ظرف کی تقدم کے ساتھ جو کہ مفید ہے اختصاص کیلئے اور لفظ مضارع کیسا تھ جو کہ خبر دینے والا ہے استمرار سے۔ غرض شارح بیان ترکیب ! و مصداق کلم طبیب خلاصہ تقریر یہ ہے کہ من حامد لکم الطبیب سے حال ہے ای کا ئنا من
And the investigation of that is that although hamd in language is an act of the tongue specifically, however, the hamd of Allah the Exalted, as stated by Imam al-Razi in his tafsir, is not the saying of a person 'I praise Allah' but rather that which implies His glorification and signifies His exaltation: from belief in His attributes of perfection, expressing that in speech, and performing actions that indicate it. So belief is the root; without it, hamd would be like an evil tree uprooted from above the earth with no stability. And action is the branch; without it, hamd would have no growth towards Allah and no acceptance with Him, like a tree without a branch and a tree without fruit. Indeed, action is the means to attain gardens and raise ranks. Allah said: 'And righteous action raises it.' And in the hadith: 'When he has no righteous action, it is not accepted.' So the author indicated that the tree of praises has a firm root, which is steadfast Islamic belief built on the knowledge of tawhid and attributes, and a branch growing towards Allah and accepted with Him, which is righteous action conforming to the pure Shariah built on the knowledge of laws and rulings. And he indicated exclusivity and continuity by His saying: 'To Him ascends the good word' by advancing the adverb indicating exclusivity and the present tense verb indicating continuity. Translation: ...
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary from the sharh of Al-Tawdih. It begins by analyzing the nature of hamd (praise) directed to Allah. While linguistically hamd is an act of the tongue, Imam al-Razi clarifies that Allah's praise is more comprehensive: it must include belief (i'tiqad) in Allah's perfect attributes, verbal expression (qawl), and righteous action ('amal). The author uses a powerful metaphor of a tree: belief is the root that gives stability, and action is the branch that bears fruit and causes growth towards Allah. Without belief, praise is like an uprooted evil tree; without action, it is like a branchless tree with no fruit. The Quranic verse 'To Him ascends the good word, and righteous action raises it' (35:10) is cited, along with a hadith that without righteous action, words of praise are not accepted. The author then explains that the phrase 'To Him ascends' indicates exclusivity (ikhtisas) by virtue of the prefixed adverb, and the present tense verb indicates continuity (dawam). The rest of the passage continues the metaphor of the tree and discusses words like 'mashari'' (watering places) for the Shariah, and the winds saba' and dabur as metaphors for the acceptance of deeds. The overall message is that praise of Allah is only complete and acceptable when it combines correct belief and righteous action in accordance with the Shariah.

Key Terms
حمد (hamd): Praise that includes belief, speech, and action directed to Allah.
كلم (kalim): Words of praise such as subhanallah, alhamdulillah, la ilaha illallah, allahu akbar.
مشارع (mashari'): Watering places; metaphor for the rulings of Shariah where believers quench their thirst for mercy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is necessary for hamd to be accepted by Allah?
A) Only verbal praise
B) Correct belief and righteous action
C) Recitation of specific phrases
D) Performing acts of charity

Key Takeaway
Praise of Allah is a comprehensive act requiring correct belief as its root and righteous action as its branch for acceptance.

Al-Quran as Source

Interpreting Kalimah Tayyibah as Praises (Mahamid) – Textual Analysis
Commentary on Quranic verse and Hadith about Kalimah Tayyibah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi usul interprets Surah Ibrahim 14:24 and the hadith on mahamid to establish that kalimah tayyibah requires both correct belief (root) and righteous deeds (branches), and distinguish between minimal and complete acceptance.

Core Idea
The good word is like a tree: faith is its root, deeds its branches; complete acceptance requires both.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih delves into the interpretation of 'kalimah tayyibah' mentioned in the Quran. The commentator explains that the good word refers to the mahamid (praises like Subhan Allah, etc.), but with a crucial condition: these words are not merely verbal; they must be rooted in correct belief (i'tiqad) and manifested in righteous deeds (a'mal salihah). The passage navigates between extreme positions—the Mu'tazilah who make deeds part of iman and thus deny any acceptance without deeds, and the Murji'ah who separate deeds entirely. The Hanafi position offers a balanced view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic Verse and Its Analogy
Locate the verse from Surah Ibrahim (14:24) and understand the simile: a good word is like a good tree. Note the two parts: root firmly fixed and branches in the sky.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah according to Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the Hadith Defining Mahamid
The hadith specifies that the 'good words' are the four praises (Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar). The commentator links these to the verse.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
3
Analyze the Tree Analogy: Root and Branches
The commentator explains that the root of the tree is faith (iman) and belief (i'tiqad), while the branches are righteous deeds (a'mal). Acceptance of the word depends on both.
This aligns with the Hanafi view that iman is tasdiq (belief) separate from deeds, but deeds are necessary for full acceptance.
4
Recognize the Hanafi Response to the Mu'tazilite Objection
The Mu'tazilah argued that since deeds are part of iman, acceptance of praise words is impossible without deeds. The Hanafi response distinguishes between complete acceptance (qabul tam) and minimal acceptance (mere validity of the utterance).
The hadith about rejection refers to complete acceptance; the words themselves are still valid worship.
5
Apply the Usul Principles: Grammatical Analysis of 'min Mahamid'
The commentator defends the interpretation by showing that the indefinite 'mahamid' can carry generality when described by a general attribute, matching the definite 'al-kalim'. This resolves the apparent conflict.
This illustrates the Hanafi usul rule that an indefinite noun can become general through context.

کا ازالہ یا استفسار کا جواب ہے استفسار یہ ہوا کہ محمد کو الکلم الطیب کی تفسیر بنایا گیا ہے یہ بیان و تفسیر بالروایت ہے یا تفسیر بالدرایت ہے دوسرے لفظوں میں یہ تفسیر ہے یا تاویل ہے تغیر نقل اور تاویل عقل سے ہوتی ہے ایک تحریف ہوتی ہے جو نہ بالدرایت ہوتی ہے نہ بالروایت بلکہ وہ با الخرص یعنی انکل کیساتھ و بقول حضرت مہتم مولانا علی محمد صاحب ( تفسیر بالڈھکوسلہ ہوتی ہے ) تو شارح اسی شبہ واستفسار کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ یہ تفسیر بالروایت ہے حدیث پیش کی نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کلمہ طیبہ کے متعلق فرمایا وہ سبحان اللہ والحمد للہ ولا الہ الا اللہ واللہ اکبر ہیں جب بندہ یہ کلمات کہتا ہے فرشتہ ان کو ذات باری تعالی کی دربار میں تحیہ کے طور پر پیش کرتا ہے اگر اس آدمی کے اور اعمال ہوتے ہیں تو یہ کلمات قبول کر لیے جاتے ہیں ورنہ مسترد کر دیئے جاتے ہیں ۔ سوال ! حضوراکرم اللہ نے صرف چار کلمات کو کلمات طیبہ کی تفسیر بنایا جس سے ان کا محدود محدود ہونا لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ اور بھی تو کلمات طیبہ ہیں کی و ۔ جواب ! مقصود حصر نہیں صرف مثال کا بیان ہے ای مثلت مثلا ۔ سوال ! حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قبولیت کلمات کیلئے اعمال صالحہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے یہ تو معتزلہ کا مذہب ہے (لا مذہب اہل السنتہ ) جو کہ اعمال کو جزو ایمان قرار دیتے ہیں۔ جواب! قبولیت سے قبولیت تامہ مراد ہے جب تک اعمال صالحہ نہ ہوں گے قبولیت تامہ نہ ہوگی۔ وانما صلح الجمع المذكر الخ. غرض شارخ جواب سوال مقدر ۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ من محامد کو الکلم کا بیان بنانا غیر صحیح ہے کیونکہ بیان و مبین و مفسر ومفتر میں مناسبت ضروری ہے جو کہ یہاں موجود نہیں ہے کیونکہ الکلم معرف بلام الاستغراق ہے وہ مستغرق تجمیع الافراد ہے اور محام جمع منکر ہے اور جمع منکر عند المصنف غیر مستغرق ہوتی ہے ( کما سیاتی ) اور مستغرق و غیر مستغرق میں تضاد و تعارض ہے فیکف یکون محمد بیانا تفسیر الکلم ۔ جواب ! (۱) من ان النكرة سے جواب اول ہے کہ ضابطہ مسلمہ ہے جب تکرہ موصوفہ ہو بصفتہ عامہ تو عموم صفت کی وجہ سے نکرہ میں بھی عموم آجاتا ہے جیسے امرائۃ کا معنی کوئی
Miskulmaleehurdu Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: ... (The passage discusses the meaning of 'good word' as praises, likening it to a good tree with roots (faith) and branches (deeds), and includes a hadith about acceptance of these words conditional upon righteous deeds, followed by grammatical questions about the phrase 'من محامد' as a hal or sifat.)
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a verse from the Quran and a related hadith, explaining the interpretation of 'kalimah tayyibah' as 'mahamid' (praises). The author begins by describing natural phenomena (winds) as metaphors for divine acceptance, then moves to the verse 'ضرب الله مثلاً كلمة طيبة كشجرة طيبة' (Ibrahim:24). He explains that the 'good word' is like a good tree: its root is faith and beliefs (i'tiqadat), and its branches are righteous deeds (a'mal). The commentary emphasizes that true praise (hamd) is not merely verbal but includes belief in Allah's attributes and acting upon that belief. The author cites Imam Razi's view that hamd requires both inward conviction and outward action. Then he quotes a hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) said the 'good words' are 'Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar,' and that a person's other righteous deeds cause these words to be accepted. This leads to questions: Does this mean acceptance is conditional on deeds (a Mu'tazilite view)? The answer distinguishes between complete acceptance (qabul tam) and mere utterance. Another question: Since 'mahamid' is indefinite plural and 'al-kalim' is definite with istighraq, how can one be an interpretation of the other? The answer uses the rule that an indefinite described by a general attribute can become general. The passage thus makes a theological and usuli point about the relationship between faith and deeds.

Key Terms
محامد (mahamid): Praiseworthy words, specifically the phrases Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar, as interpreted in the hadith.
كلمہ طیبہ (kalimah tayyibah): The good word, interpreted in this passage as the mahamid (praises) with faith as root and deeds as branches.
قبول تام (qabul tam): Complete acceptance, which requires both utterance of praise and righteous deeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what happens to the praises (mahamid) of a person who has no other righteous deeds?
A) They are completely accepted because they are good words.
B) They are rejected entirely and the person becomes a disbeliever.
C) They are rejected in the sense of not being fully accepted, but the person remains a believer.
D) They are accepted but with a reduced reward.

Key Takeaway
The good word (kalimah tayyibah) is like a good tree: it requires both faith (root) and righteous deeds (branches) for complete acceptance, but the utterance itself remains valid even without other deeds, according to the Hanafi usul.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
Interpreting Al-Kalim al-Tayyib: Tafsir bi Riwaya vs. Tafsir bi Diraya
Commentary on interpreting 'al-kalim al-tayyib' with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the distinction between tafsir bi riwaya and tafsir bi diraya and explain why the interpretation of 'al-kalim al-tayyib' as the four phrases is based on transmitted hadith.

Core Idea
Al-Kalim al-Tayyib is interpreted by transmitted hadith, not personal opinion; acceptance requires deeds but incomplete acceptance is possible.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a key usul al-fiqh concern: is the interpretation of a Quranic phrase based on transmitted report (riwaya) or rational opinion (diraya)? He cites a hadith to show it is riwaya, and then answers objections about limitation and the requirement of deeds for acceptance. This lesson unpacks the hadith evidence and the Hanafi response to the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central doubt
The inquiry is whether the interpretation of 'al-kalim al-tayyib' as 'mahamid' is by transmission (riwaya) or by reason (diraya).
This is a key usul distinction: tafsir bi riwaya relies on transmitted sources; tafsir bi diraya involves personal reasoning.
2
Examine the hadith cited
The Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly states that al-kalim al-tayyib is Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar. This is the proof that the interpretation is tafsir bi riwaya.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but still binding in fiqh and acceptable for interpretation.
3
Analyze the objection of limitation
The objector says: the hadith mentions only four phrases, implying that only those are good words. The commentator answers that the purpose is not limitation (hasr) but merely giving an example.
This shows that the hadith specifies the minimum, not an exhaustive list.
4
Analyze the Mu'tazila objection
The hadith says words are accepted only if there are deeds. The Mu'tazila claim this proves deeds are part of faith. The commentator rebuts: 'acceptance' here means complete acceptance (qabul tamm); without deeds, superficial acceptance occurs but not full.
Hanafis distinguish between the essence of faith (tasdiq) and its perfection (kamil).
5
Derive the usul principle
A hadith, even if ahad, can serve as a bayan (clarification) for a mujmal (ambiguous) Quranic phrase. This principle allows specification of general Quranic texts by transmitted reports.
This is a foundational Hanafi usul rule.
