شرح تلویح قوله واصول الفقه ماسبق كان بيان مفهوم اصول الفقه الخ ۔ غرض شارح تو ضیح متن ہے کہ مصنف نے اب تک جو کچھ بیان کیا وہ اصول فقہ کا مفہوم اور معنی تھا اب اس کا مصداق بیان کر رہے ہیں اصول فقہ کے مصداق کی انواع چار قسموں میں منحصر ہے (کتاب، ستہ، اجماع ، قیاس ) اور یہ انحصار بحکم الاستقراء ہے یعنی حصر استقرائی ہے ووجه ضبطہ سے شارح اقسام اور بعد کی دو وجہ حصر بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ وجہ حصر اول ! یہ بت کہ دلیل شرعی یا وحی ہوگی یا غیر وحی اگر وحی ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں وحی متلو ہوگی یا غیر متلوا گر متلو ہے تو کتاب اگر غیر متلو ہے تو یہ اگر وحی نہیں ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں عصر واحد ( ایک زمانہ ) کے کل اور تمام لوگوں کا قول ہوگا یا بعض کا اول اجماع اور ثانی ' قیاس ہے۔ وجہ حصہ دوم اوجہ حصر ثانی یہ ہے کہ دلیل شرعی ہم تک یا رسول اللہ کے ذریعہ سے پہنچی ہوگی یا کسی اور ذریعہ سے اگر رسول اللہ کے ذریعہ سے پہنچی ہے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو اس دلیل کے الفاظ اور نظم کے ساتھ اعجاز متعلق ہو گا یعنی اس دلیل کے الفاظ معجز ہوں گے یا نہ اگر معجز ہیں تو کتاب اللہ ورنہ ستہ اور اگر وہ دلیل شرعی نبی کریم کے واسطہ سے ہم تک نہیں پہنچی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو وہ دلیل ایسے لوگوں سے صادر ہوئی ہوگی جن میں عصمت عن الخطا و شرط ہے یا نہ اول صورت میں اجماع ہے ثانی صورت میں قیاس۔ فائدہ! (۱) ۔ ایک اور وجہ حصر بھی بیان کی گئی ہے جو شارح نے ذکر نہیں کی وہ حسب ذیل ہے کہ دلیل شرعی مظہر حکم ہوگی یا مثبت حکم اگر مظہر ہے تو قیاس اگر مثبت ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں من جانب الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ہوگی یا من غیرہ ہوگی ۔ اگر من غیرہ ہے تو اجماع اگر من جانب الرسول ہو تو پواسطہ جبرائیل ہوگی یا نہ اول کتاب ثانی سنہ ۔ فائدہ ! (۲)۔ وحی متلو کی متعدد کی گئی ہیں (۱) وحی متلو وہ ہے جس کے الفاظ تلاوت کیے جائیں اور تلاوت الفاظ موجب ثواب ہو جیسے الفاظ القرآن کی تلاوت (۲) وحی متلو وہ ہے جس کے الفاظ کی تلاوت پر احکام جاری ہوں مثلاً حائض و جنبی پر عدم تلاوت قرآن کا علم اور نماز میں اس کی تلاوت کے وجوب کا حکم حائض اور جنبی اور محدث کیلئے مس قرآن کا حکم وغیرہ (۳) وحی متلووہ ہے جس کو حضرت جبرائیل نے آپ کی ہے تلاوت کیا ہو اور آپ نے امت پر تلاوت کیا ہو۔ فائدہ ! (۳)۔ انکان قول کل الامتہ، سے عامتہ الناس مراد نہیں ہیں کیونکہ عامتہ الناس کا اجماع کسی مسئلہ پر شرعا حجت نہیں ہے بلکہ اس سے مراد کل علماء مجتہدین فی عصر واحد کا قول ہے ۔ فائدہ! (۲) ان اشترط عصمة من صدر عنه فالاجماع الخ، عصمت سے مراد عصمت مجتہد من عن المعصیات والمنکرات نہیں ہے کیونکہ اجتماع میں یہ شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ عصمت سے مراد عصمت عن الخطاء والضلالہ فی هذا الحلم الجمع علیہ ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے لا جمع امتی علی الصلالة - واما شرائع من قبلنا الخ غرض شارح جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے ادلہ اصول فقہ کو اقسام اربعہ میں منحصر کیا ہے یہ حصر باطل ہے بلکہ ادلہ اصول فقہ چار سے زیادہ ہیں کیونکہ فقہ کا اصل وہ ہوتا ہے جس سے حکم ثابت ہو اور حکم فقط ان چار سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اور بھی بہت ساری اشیاء ہیں جن سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے (۱) شرائع من قبلنا (ہم سے سابق انبیاء کی شرائع ) بھی بعض احکام ثابت ہوئے ہیں جو ہم پر لازم ہیں مثلا وكتبنا عليهم فيها ان النفس بالنفس الخ، تو راہ کا حکم ہے ہم پر لازم ہے اسی طرح امام شافعی وغیرہ جو بیع السلم فی الحیوان کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ بیان اوصاف سے حیوان متعین ہو جاتا ہے وہ تھا ۔ بقرہ موسی علیہ السلام سے استدلال کرتے ہیں کہ وہ بقرۃ اوصاف کے بیان کرنے سے متعین ہوگئی تھی اسی طرح شوافع غیر مال مثل تعلیم زراعت در می غنم کے گھر بنانے کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں دلیل میں قصہ نکاح موسی علیہ السلام بنت شعیب علیہ السلام پیش کرتے ہیں انہوں نے رعی غنم کو گھر مقرر کیا تھا بہر حال شرائع من قبلنا سے بھی احکام ثابت ہوتے ہیں تو وہ بھی ایک دلیل شرعی بن گئے (۲) تعامل اہل اسلام (جس میں عوام خواص سب عامل ہوں) سے بھی بسا اوقات حکم ثابت ہو جاتا ہے مثلا ایسی چیز کی بیع کرلی جس میں مبیع. معدوم ہے جیسے جو تا چار پائی وغیرہ حالانکہ مبیع معدوم ہو تو بیع باطل ہے لیکن تمام اہل اسلام کا تعامل ہے اس لیے اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا اسی طرح آج کل ضاد کو بصوت دال پڑھنا اس پر تعامل ہے ( کما یقرءقراء السعودیہ والمصریہ وغیرھا ) اس کو مفسد صلوۃ نہیں قرار دیا گیا تو تعامل سے احکام ثابت ہو رہے ہیں اس لئے کہ تعامل بھی ایک دلیل شرعی ہوگی (۳) قول صحابی سے بھی احکام ثابت ہوتے ہیں تو وہ بھی ایک دلیل شرعی بن گیا کما قال رسول اللہ اللہ علیکم بسنتی وسنه الخلفا الرائدین ، اصحابی کالنجوم با هم اقتدیتم احمد یتیم (۴) معقول بھی ایک دلیل ہے معقول سے مراد دلیل عقلی ہے اس کو استدلال بھی کہا جاتا ہے بعض " حضرات اس کو دلیل خامس بناتے ہیں جیسا کہ صاحب ہدایہ کا طرز ہے ہر مسئلہ شرعیہ پر ایک دلیل نقلی پیش کر کے بعد دلیل عقلی پیش کرتا ہے اسی طرح امام طحاوی نظر پیش کر کے اس سے حکم ثابت کرتا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دلیل عقلی ( معقول ) بھی ایک دلیل شرعی ہے اس سے بھی احکام ثابت ہوتے ہیں ونحو ذالک اس میں بہت ساری اشیاء داخل ہیں مثلا استصحاب حال کبھی استصحاب سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے استصحاب کا معنی یہ ہے کہ حال کو باضی کا قرین بنادیا جائے باعتبار الحکم ( حال کا حکم ماضی کے مطابق ) جعل حکم الحال قریب نہ علی الماضی مثلا مکری (کرایہ پر دینے والا ) کہتا ہے کہ چونکہ گذشتہ مہینہ کارخانہ چلتا رہا ہے اس
Commentary of Talwih: His saying 'and usul al-fiqh whatever preceded was an explanation of the concept of usul al-fiqh, etc.' The purpose of the commentator of Tawdih is that whatever the author has explained so far was the meaning and concept of usul al-fiqh; now he is stating its referent. The types of the referent of usul al-fiqh are confined to four categories: (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas). And this confinement is by way of istiqra' (induction), meaning an inductive limitation. By 'wajh dabitihi' the commentator explains the categories and afterwards two proofs of the limitation. First proof of limitation: The legal proof is either wahy (revelation) or non-wahy. If it is wahy, then two possibilities: either wahy matluw (recited revelation) or non-matluw. If it is matluw, then it is the Book; if non-matluw, then it is the Sunnah. If it is not wahy, then two possibilities: it is either the saying of all the people of one era or some of them. The first is Ijma' and the second is Qiyas. Second proof of limitation: The legal proof reaches us either through the Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.) or through some other means. If it reaches through the Messenger, then two possibilities: either the words and arrangement of that proof are associated with i'jaz (miraculousness), i.e., the words of that proof are miraculous, or not. If they are miraculous, then it is the Book of Allah; otherwise, it is the Sunnah. If the legal proof does not reach us through the Prophet (s.a.w.), then two possibilities: either that proof emanated from people in whom 'ismah (infallibility from error) is [assumed] as a condition, or not. In the first case it is Ijma', in the second it is Qiyas. Benefit 1: Another proof of limitation has also been stated which the commentator did not mention: the legal proof is either a manifestation of the ruling or an establisher of the ruling. If it is a manifestation, then Qiyas; if it is an establisher, then two possibilities: it is from the side of the Messenger (s.a.w.) or from others. If from others, then Ijma'; if from the side of the Messenger, then either through Jibril or not; first is Book, second is Sunnah. Benefit 2: Wahy matluw has been given multiple definitions: (1) Wahy matluw is that whose words are recited and whose recitation brings reward, like the recitation of the words of the Quran. (2) Wahy matluw is that upon whose words rulings are based, e.g., the prohibition of recitation for a menstruating woman or junub, and the obligation of its recitation in prayer, and the ruling of touching the Quran for the menstruating, junub, and those without wudu, etc. (3) Wahy matluw is that which Jibril recited to the Prophet and the Prophet recited to the Ummah. Benefit 3: 'The saying of the entire Ummah' does not mean the general public, because the consensus of the general public on any issue is not a legal proof; rather it means the saying of all the mujtahid scholars in one era. Benefit 2: 'If 'ismah is required in the one from whom it emanates, then Ijma', etc. 'Ismah here does not mean the infallibility of the mujtahid from sins and evil deeds, because that condition is not present in consensus; rather, 'ismah here means infallibility from error and misguidance in that ruling upon which the consensus is formed. The Prophet's noble saying: 'My Ummah will not unite on error.' And as for the laws of those before us' – The purpose of the commentator is to answer an implied objection. Objection: You have confined the proofs of usul al-fiqh to four categories. This confinement is false; rather the proofs of usul al-fiqh are more than four, because the basis of fiqh is that from which a ruling is established, and a ruling is not established only from these four, but there are many other things from which rulings are established: (1) The laws of those before us (shara'i' man qablana) – some rulings are established from them that are binding upon us, e.g., 'And We prescribed for them therein that a life for a life' – the ruling of the Torah is binding upon us. Similarly, al-Shafi'i and others who permit salam in animals argue that describing the specific features makes the animal specified, citing the cow of Musa (a.s.). Similarly, the Shafi'is permit non-wealth such as teaching agriculture, building a house in return for shepherding sheep, citing the story of Musa's marriage to the daughter of Shu'ayb, where he appointed shepherding sheep as a payment. So rulings are established from shara'i' man qablana, thus they become a legal proof. (2) The practice of the people of Islam (ta'amul ahl al-Islam) – sometimes rulings are established from it, e.g., selling something where the sold item is non-existent, like a cot or bed, even though if the sold item is non-existent the sale is void, but the entire practice of the people of Islam (including common and elite) is such, so it is deemed permissible. Similarly, today pronouncing 'dad' with the sound of 'dal' – there is practice on this (as read by the reciters of Saudi and Egypt, etc.) and it is not considered invalidating of prayer. So rulings are established from ta'amul, thus ta'amul is also a legal proof. (3) The saying of a Companion – rulings are established from it, so it becomes a legal proof, as the Prophet said: 'Adhere to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the rightly guided caliphs'; 'My Companions are like stars; whichever you follow, you will be guided.' (4) 'Aql (reason) – it is also a proof. 'Aql means rational proof; it is also called istidlal. Some scholars make it a fifth proof; as the author of al-Hidayah does – for every legal issue he presents a transmitted proof and then a rational proof. Similarly, Imam al-Tahawi presents rational arguments and establishes rulings from them. So it is known that rational proof is also a legal proof; rulings are established from it. 'And the like of that' includes many things, e.g., istishab al-hal – sometimes a ruling is established from istishab. The meaning of istishab is to make the present state a companion to the past with respect to the ruling (the ruling of the present is according to the past), i.e., to make the ruling of the present follow the past. For example, the lessor says that since the factory continued running in the past month, this

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, explaining the concept of usul al-fiqh and its sources. The author first clarifies that the previous discussion was about the meaning of usul al-fiqh; now he is discussing its referent (musdaq). The referent of usul al-fiqh is confined to four types: the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, Ijma' (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy). This confinement is based on istiqra' (induction), meaning a comprehensive survey of the revealed sources leads to the conclusion that only these four are the primary proofs. The author then provides two rational proofs (wajh hasr) to justify this limitation.

The first proof proceeds by dividing all legal proofs into revelation (wahy) or non-revelation. Revelation is either recited (matluw, i.e., the Quran) or non-recited (the Sunnah). Non-revelation is either the consensus of all mujtahids of one era (ijma') or the opinion of some (qiyas). The second proof divides proofs based on how they reach us: either through the Prophet or not. If through the Prophet, then either miraculous in wording (Quran) or not (Sunnah). If not through the Prophet, then either from an infallible source (ijma') or not (qiyas).

The commentator also adds a third proof not mentioned by the original author: the proof either manifests the ruling (qiyas) or establishes it. If it establishes, it is either from the Prophet (through Jibril = Quran, or without = Sunnah) or from others (ijma').

Then, several benefits (fawa'id) are discussed: definitions of wahy matluw, clarification that 'ijma' refers to the consensus of mujtahid scholars, not the general public, and that 'ismah in ijma' means infallibility from error, not from sins.

Finally, the commentator addresses an objection: there are more than four proofs, citing examples: the laws of previous prophets (shara'i' man qablana), the consistent practice of the Muslim community (ta'amul ahl al-Islam), the sayings of Companions, and rational proof ('aql). For each, the objector provides examples, including the Shafi'i use of the story of Musa's cow for salam in animals, and the Hanafi reliance on the practice of Muslims allowing sale of non-existent items. The passage implies that these are indeed sources of law, but the Hanafi position usually considers them secondary or included under the four main sources (e.g., qiyas includes rational proof, istishab is a type of evidence). The commentator does not give a full response here but sets up the objection to be answered later.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta'amul): The consistent practice of the Muslim community, including both common people and scholars.
استصحاب (istishab): A presumption that the previous state continues until evidence of change; a tool for establishing rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as an objection in the passage?
A) Laws of previous prophets
B) Practice of the Muslim community
C) Sayings of the Companions
D) Consensus of the general public

Key Takeaway
Objections to the four-source limitation are met by showing that additional proofs are either included under the four or are secondary; the primary sources of usul al-fiqh remain four.

Al-Quran as Source
advanced
10 min
The Exhaustiveness of the Four Sources: Responding to Objections
Refuting claims that other sources are independent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are exhaustive and evaluate the status of other potential sources like pre-Islamic laws, practice, etc.

Core Idea
All alleged additional proofs are subsumed under the four; no independent fifth source exists.

This passage addresses a common objection: if many things (pre-Islamic laws, Muslim practice, companion statements, reason, etc.) seem to establish rulings, why restrict the sources to four? The Hanafi response, following al-Taftazani, shows that each of these is reducible to one of the four primary sources. Understanding this subsumption is key to maintaining a coherent usul framework.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objector's claim
Identify the examples the objector uses to argue that the four-source classification is incomplete. These include shara'i' qablana, ta'amul, qawl sahabi, ma'qul, istishab, custom, lots, physiognomy, etc.
Note that the objector points to real fiqh applications where these seem to produce rulings.
2
State the Hanafi response for each example
For each claimed source, the commentator shows it is not independent but falls under one of the four. For instance, pre-Islamic laws mentioned in Quran or Sunnah without disapproval are followed as Quranic or Sunnah rulings, not as independent proofs.
Focus on the reasoning: why each cannot stand alone.
3
Grasp the principle of subsumption
A source is independent only if it provides a ruling without relying on Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas. All the objector's examples ultimately derive their authority from one of these four.
This is the core of the Hanafi defense.
4
Distinguish independent from subsidiary sources
Recognize that the Hanafi position does not deny that these sources are used; it denies they are independent. Knowing this distinction prevents confusion in usul methodology.
It also clarifies debates with other schools.

(۲) ان اشترط عصمة من صدر عنه فالاجماع الخ، عصمت سے مراد عصمت مجتہد من عن المعصیات والمنکرات نہیں ہے کیونکہ اجتماع میں یہ شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ عصمت سے مراد عصمت عن الخطاء والضلالہ فی هذا الحلم الجمع علیہ ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے لا جمع امتی علی الصلالة - واما شرائع من قبلنا الخ غرض شارح جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے ادلہ اصول فقہ کو اقسام اربعہ میں منحصر کیا ہے یہ حصر باطل ہے بلکہ ادلہ اصول فقہ چار سے زیادہ ہیں کیونکہ فقہ کا اصل وہ ہوتا ہے جس سے حکم ثابت ہو اور حکم فقط ان چار سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اور بھی بہت ساری اشیاء ہیں جن سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے (۱) شرائع من قبلنا (ہم سے سابق انبیاء کی شرائع ) بھی بعض احکام ثابت ہوئے ہیں جو ہم پر لازم ہیں مثلا وكتبنا عليهم فيها ان النفس بالنفس الخ، تو راہ کا حکم ہے ہم پر لازم ہے اسی طرح امام شافعی وغیرہ جو بیع السلم فی الحیوان کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ بیان اوصاف سے حیوان متعین ہو جاتا ہے وہ تھا ۔ بقرہ موسی علیہ السلام سے استدلال کرتے ہیں کہ وہ بقرۃ اوصاف کے بیان کرنے سے متعین ہوگئی تھی اسی طرح شوافع غیر مال مثل تعلیم زراعت در می غنم کے گھر بنانے کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں دلیل میں قصہ نکاح موسی علیہ السلام بنت شعیب علیہ السلام پیش کرتے ہیں انہوں نے رعی غنم کو گھر مقرر کیا تھا بہر حال شرائع من قبلنا سے بھی احکام ثابت ہوتے ہیں تو وہ بھی ایک دلیل شرعی بن گئے (۲) تعامل اہل اسلام (جس میں عوام خواص سب عامل ہوں) سے بھی بسا اوقات حکم ثابت ہو جاتا ہے مثلا ایسی چیز کی بیع کرلی جس میں مبیع. معدوم ہے جیسے جو تا چار پائی وغیرہ حالانکہ مبیع معدوم ہو تو بیع باطل ہے لیکن تمام اہل اسلام کا تعامل ہے اس لیے اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا اسی طرح آج کل ضاد کو بصوت دال پڑھنا اس پر تعامل ہے ( کما یقرءقراء السعودیہ والمصریہ وغیرھا ) اس کو مفسد صلوۃ نہیں قرار دیا گیا تو تعامل سے احکام ثابت ہو رہے ہیں اس لئے کہ تعامل بھی ایک دلیل شرعی ہوگی (۳) قول صحابی سے بھی احکام ثابت ہوتے ہیں تو وہ بھی ایک دلیل شرعی بن گیا کما قال رسول اللہ اللہ علیکم بسنتی وسنه الخلفا الرائدین ، اصحابی کالنجوم با هم اقتدیتم احمد یتیم (۴) معقول بھی ایک دلیل ہے معقول سے مراد دلیل عقلی ہے اس کو استدلال بھی کہا جاتا ہے بعض حضرات اس کو دلیل خامس بناتے ہیں جیسا کہ صاحب ہدایہ کا طرز ہے ہر مسئلہ شرعیہ پر ایک دلیل نقلی پیش کر کے بعد دلیل عقلی پیش کرتا ہے اسی طرح امام طحاوی نظر پیش کر کے اس سے حکم ثابت کرتا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دلیل عقلی ( معقول ) بھی ایک دلیل شرعی ہے اس سے بھی احکام ثابت ہوتے ہیں ونحو ذالک اس میں بہت ساری اشیاء داخل ہیں مثلا استصحاب حال کبھی استصحاب سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے استصحاب کا معنی یہ ہے کہ حال کو باضی کا قرین بنادیا جائے باعتبار الحکم ( حال کا حکم ماضی کے مطابق ) جعل حکم الحال قریب نہ علی الماضی مثلا مکری (کرایہ پر دینے والا ) کہتا ہے کہ چونکہ گذشتہ مہینہ کارخانہ چلتا رہا ہے اس لئے کرایہ دینا ہو گا مکتری ( کرایہ پر لینے والا ) کہتا ہے نہیں چلا لہذا کرایہ نہیں دوں گا اب حال کو دیکھا جائے گا اگر فی الحال چل رہا ہے تو حکم لگایا جائے گا کہ ماضی میں بھی چلتا رہا والا فلا تو استصحاب حال بھی ایک دلیل ۔ ہے جس سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے (۲) کبھی عرف سے بھی حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے (۳) کبھی قرعہ سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے (۴) کبھی قیافہ سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے (۵) کبھی تحری سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ اگر قبلہ معلوم نہ ہو تو تحجری سے معلوم کیا جائے گا (1) اخذ بالظاہر ( ۷ ) اخذ بالاحتیاط وغیرہ یہ تمام امور ایسے ہیں کہ ان سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے تو یہ بھی اولہ شرعیہ کہلانے کے مستحق میں حضر ادلہ شرعیہ فی الاربعہ باطل ہے جواب اشارح تفتازانی جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ حصر بالکل صحیح ہے ادلہ مستقلہ و کامل بلا حکام صرف چارہی ہیں باقی جن کے ساتھ اشکال پیش کیا گیا ہے یہ مستقل اولہ نہیں بلکہ انہیں ادلہ اربعہ میں داخل ہیں (۱) اگر شرائع من قبلنا قرآن وحدیث میں مذکور نہیں تو وہ ہمارے لیے حجت نہیں ہیں اگر قرآن و سنت میں مذکور ہیں تو دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو انکار و مذمت کے ساتھ ہوں گی یا بلا انکار اگر انکا رو ندمت کے ساتھ ہیں وہ بھی ہمارے لیے حجت نہیں جیسے وعلی الذین ھاد و احر منا کل ذی ظفر الا یہ آخر میں فرمایا ذالک جزینا هم فیهم الخ اگر شرائع من قبلنا کتاب وستہ میں مذکور ہیں بلا انکار و بلا ندمت تو وہ ہمارے لیے حجت ہیں لیکن بائیں حیثیت کہ وہ کتاب اللہ کا حکم ہیں یا بائیں حیثیت کہ وہ ستہ بینا ہیں نہ کہ بایں حیثیت کہ وہ انبیاء سابقہ کی شریعت اور حکم نہیں لہذا یہ کوئی مستقل دلیل نہیں ہے بلکہ داخل فی القرآن یا داخل فی السنتہ ہیں (۲) تعامل اہل اسلام بھی کوئی مستقل دلیل شرعی نہیں ہے. بلکہ راجع الی الاجماع ہے بشرطیکہ تعامل بین القرون الفاضلہ ہو (۳) قول صحابی بھی مستقل دلیل نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر قول صحابی مدرک بالقیاس ہے تو قیاس میں داخل ہے اگر غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہے تو سماع پر موقوف ہو کر داخل فی السنہ ہے (۴) اسی طرح معقول و دلیل عقلی جس کو بعض حضرات نے دلیل خامس کا نام دیا ہے اور اسکا نام استدلال رکھا ہے یہ بھی کوئی مستقل دلیل نہیں ہے کیونکہ عقل محض اور عقل خالص سے کوئی حکم شرعی ثابت نہیں ہوسکتا تو لازما اس دلیل عقلی کو یا تو کتاب اللہ سے اخذ کیا گیا ہوگا یا حدیث سے تو یہ بھی ان میں داخل ہو جائے گی (۵) عرف تعامل کی طرح اجتماع میں داخل ہے (۶) استصحاب حال یہ ملحق با السنتہ ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے۔ دع ما یر بک الی مالایز بیک (۷) قرعه عند الاحناف حجہ نہیں عند الشوافع حجت ہو کر داخل فی السنتہ ہے کما روی انہ علیه السلام يقرع بین نساء عند الخروج الى سفر الخ (۸) قیافه عند الاحناف مجمہ نہیں عند الشوافع داخل في الستة ہے (۹) تحری داخل فی سبیہ ہے کیونکہ تحری میں شہادت قلب ہوتی ہے تو یہ استفتاء قلب والی حدیث پر عمل ہو گا (۱۰) اخذ بالاحتیاط میں عمل اقوی دلیلین ہوتا ہے تو یہ بھی کتاب یاستہ یا اجماع کے ساتھ ہی عمل ہوگا (۱۱) اخذ بالظاہر میں ظاہر دلیل پر عمل ہوتا ہے تو وہ دلیل یا کتاب ہوگی یاستہ یا اجماع لہذا یہ تمام دلائل انہیں ادلہ اربعہ کے تحت داخل نہیں کوئی مستقل دلیل نہیں۔ فائدہ ! (1) . قیاس اور معقول میں چند فروق ہیں (۱) قیاس میں علت مستنبطہ ضروری ہے جع کہ معقول میں ضروری نہیں ہے
The consensus of the common people on any issue is not a legal proof; rather it means the statement of all mujtahids in one era. Benefit: (2) He stipulated infallibility from the one from whom it emanates, so the consensus... Infallibility does not mean infallibility of the mujtahid from sins and evil deeds, because this condition is not present in consensus; rather infallibility here means infallibility from error and misguidance in this ruling upon which consensus is formed. The Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'My community will not gather on error.' And as for the laws of those before us... The purpose of the commentator is to answer an implicit question. The question is: You have restricted the proofs of usul al-fiqh to four categories; this restriction is invalid, because the proofs of usul al-fiqh are more than four. The foundation of fiqh is that from which a ruling is established, and rulings are not established only from these four; rather there are many other things from which rulings are established: (1) The laws of those before us (shara'i' man qablana) also establish some rulings that are binding on us, for example: 'And We prescribed for them therein that a life for a life' (Quran 5:45). So the law of retaliation is binding on us. Similarly, Imam al-Shafi'i and others who permit salam sale of animals argue that describing the qualities makes the animal specific; they use the cow of Musa (peace be upon him) as evidence that that cow became specific through the description of its qualities. Likewise, the Shafi'is permit compensation in kind such as teaching agriculture or using a sheepfold as a house, citing the story of the marriage of Musa with the daughter of Shu'ayb (peace be upon them), where he set the sheepfold as a house. In any case, rulings are established from the laws of those before us, so they also become a legal proof. (2) The practice of the people of Islam (ta'amul ahl al-Islam), in which both commoners and elites act, also sometimes establishes a ruling. For example, selling something in which the sold item is non-existent, like a cot or a bed, although if the sold item is non-existent the sale is void, but because the practice of all Muslims is to do so, it has been deemed permissible. Similarly, nowadays reading the letter ضاد with the sound of دال is a practice (as read by Saudi and Egyptian reciters, etc.), and it is not considered invalidating of prayer. So rulings are established from practice, because practice is also a legal proof. (3) The statement of a Companion also establishes rulings, so it becomes a legal proof, as the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Hold fast to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs,' and 'My companions are like stars; whomever you follow, you will be guided.' (4) Reason (ma'qul) is also a proof. By reason is meant rational proof, also called istidlal. Some people make it a fifth proof, as the author of al-Hidayah does by presenting a transmitted proof for every legal issue followed by a rational proof. Similarly, Imam al-Tahawi presents a rational consideration and establishes a ruling from it. This shows that rational proof is also a legal proof, and from it also rulings are established. And the like thereof includes many things, for example: istishab al-hal. Sometimes a ruling is established from istishab. The meaning of istishab is that the present is made analogous to the past with regard to the ruling. For example, the lessor says: 'Since the factory has been running for the past month, rent must be paid.' The lessee says: 'No, it wasn't running, so I won't pay rent.' Now the present is examined: if it is currently running, it is ruled that it was also running in the past. So istishab al-hal is also a proof from which a ruling is established. (2) Sometimes a ruling is established from custom ('urf). (3) Sometimes a ruling is established from casting lots (qur'ah). (4) Sometimes a ruling is established from physiognomy (qiyafah). (5) Sometimes a ruling is established from ijtihad (taharri), such as when the direction of the qibla is unknown, it is determined through ijtihad. (6) Acting upon what is apparent (akhdh bi al-zahir), (7) Acting upon precaution (akhdh bi al-ihtiyat). All such matters are such that rulings are established from them, so they also deserve to be called legal proofs. Therefore, restricting legal proofs to four is invalid. The answer: The commentator al-Taftazani answers that the restriction is completely correct; the independent and complete proofs for rulings are only four. The rest of the things with which objection has been made are not independent proofs but are subsumed under the four proofs. (1) If the laws of those before us are not mentioned in the Quran and Hadith, then they are not proof for us. If they are mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah, then there are two cases: either they are mentioned with disapproval and condemnation, or without disapproval. If they are with disapproval and condemnation, then they are also not proof for us, like the verse: 'And to those who are Jews, We prohibited every animal with an undivided hoof...' (Quran 6:146) and He said: 'That We recompensed them...' If the laws are mentioned in the Book and Sunnah without disapproval and without condemnation, then they are proof for us, but not by virtue of being the law of the previous prophets, but by virtue of being the ruling of the Book of Allah or the Sunnah of His Prophet. Therefore it is not an independent proof but is subsumed under the Quran or Sunnah. (2) The practice of the people of Islam is also not an independent legal proof; rather it reverts to consensus, provided that the practice occurred in the virtuous generations. (3) The statement of a Companion is also not an independent proof; rather if the Companion's statement is based on analogy, it is subsumed under qiyas; if it is not based on analogy, it is based on hearing and thus subsumed under the Sunnah. (4) Similarly, reason and rational proof, which some have called the fifth proof and named istidlal, is neither an independent proof, because from bare reason and pure intellect no legal ruling can be established. So necessarily this rational proof is either derived from the Book of Allah or from the Hadith, so it will be subsumed under them. (5) Custom, like practice, is subsumed under consensus. (6) Istishab al-hal is attached to the Sunnah. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' (7) Casting lots is not a proof according to the Hanafis; according to the Shafi'is it is a proof and is subsumed under the Sunnah, as it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) would cast lots between his wives when going on a journey, etc. (8) Physiognomy is not a proof according to the Hanafis; according to the Shafi'is it is subsumed under the Sunnah. (9) Ijtihad (taharri) is subsumed under the Sunnah, because ijtihad involves the testimony of the heart, so it is acting upon the hadith of consulting the heart. (10) Acting upon precaution (akhdh bi al-ihtiyat) involves acting upon the stronger of two proofs, so it is acting with the Book, Sunnah, or consensus. (11) Acting upon what is apparent involves acting upon an apparent proof, so that proof is either the Book, Sunnah, or consensus. Therefore, all these proofs are subsumed under the four proofs; none is an independent proof. Benefit: (1) There are several differences between qiyas and reason (ma'qul): (1) In qiyas, an extracted cause (illah mustanbitah) is necessary, whereas in reason it is not necessary.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the exhaustiveness of the four sources of Islamic law. The commentator (Miskin al-Malih, quoting al-Taftazani) responds to an objection: the four-source structure (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) seems incomplete because many other things seem to produce legal rulings. The objector lists: pre-Islamic laws (shara'i' man qablana), the practice of Muslims (ta'amul), the statement of a Companion (qawl sahabi), rational proof (ma'qul/istidlal), istishab (presumption of continuity), custom ('urf), casting lots (qur'ah), physiognomy (qiyafah), ijtihad (taharri), acting on appearances (akhdh bi al-zahir), and acting on precaution (akhdh bi al-ihtiyat). The Hanafi response, attributed to al-Taftazani, argues that all these are not independent but are subsumed under the four. Pre-Islamic laws are only proof if adopted by Quran or Sunnah; practice of Muslims, if from virtuous generations, is part of ijma; statements of Companions are either qiyas or sunnah; rational proof must derive from revelation; custom reverts to consensus; istishab is from the sunnah (the hadith about leaving doubt); casting lots and physiognomy are either not accepted (Hanafi) or part of sunnah (Shafi'i); ijtihad is sunnah; precaution and appearance-based rulings operate with the stronger proof from the four. Thus the four-source classification is comprehensive. The passage ends with a note distinguishing qiyas from reason (ma'qul): qiyas requires an identified effective cause ('illah), whereas reason does not. This is a typical Hanafi usul defense against the Mutakallimin who might consider more sources.

Key Terms
شرائع من قبلنا (Sharā‘i‘ man qablanā): The religious laws of previous prophets revealed before Prophet Muhammad ﷺ.
تعامل اهل الإسلام (Ta‘āmul ahl al-Islām): The prevalent practice of Muslims, including both commoners and elite, in a particular matter.
قول الصحابي (Qawl al-Ṣaḥābī): A statement or opinion of a Companion of the Prophet ﷺ.
معقول (Ma‘qūl): Rational proof or reason-based argument used in fiqh; also called istidlal.
استصحاب حال (Istiṣḥāb al-ḥāl): Presumption that a state of affairs continues until evidence shows otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the status of the statement of a Companion (qawl sahabi) as a legal proof?
A) It is an independent proof because the Prophet ﷺ said 'My companions are like stars.'
B) It is subsumed under the Quran because companions knew the Quran best.
C) It is subsumed under either qiyas or sunnah, depending on whether it is based on analogy or direct hearing.
D) It is not a proof at all because companions were fallible.

Key Takeaway
Any potential source beyond the four (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) is not independent; its authority derives from one of these four.

Al-Quran as Source
advanced
12 min
Taftazani's Critique of Hukm and Thubut Definitions
Critical refinement of the definition of hukm and thubut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible definitions of hukm and explain how each affects the meaning of thubut in the context of proofs.

Core Idea
Hukm as Allah's address is eternal and not provable; hukm as established by address relies on proofs yielding only predominant opinion.

This lesson examines a critical refinement by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani regarding the definition of 'hukm' (ruling) and 'thubut' (proof/establishment) in usul al-fiqh. The matn of al-Tawdih made an ambiguous statement, and Taftazani exposes its lack of fruitfulness. Understanding this critique sharpens your ability to distinguish between the ontological status of divine speech and the epistemological value of textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Definitions of Hukm
From the passage, extract the two possible meanings of 'hukm': (1) the address of Allah (khitab Allah), and (2) what is established by that address (ma thabat bi al-khitab). Note the author's framing in the matn that sparked Taftazani's critique.
These definitions lead to different implications for how we understand 'thubut' (being proven).
2
Analyze the First Definition and Its Consequence
If hukm is Allah's address (khitab), it is eternal (qadim) and cannot be 'proven' by textual evidences. Thubut can only mean our knowledge of the ruling from the proofs, not its reality in itself. Recognize that this makes the phrase 'proof of the ruling' problematic.
This aligns with the Hanafi doctrine of the Quran being uncreated.
3
Analyze the Second Definition and Its Consequence
If hukm means what is established by the address, then 'thubut' from proofs refers to the process of establishing the ruling. However, not all proofs yield certainty. The three main proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) do yield certainty, but qiyas (analogy) yields only ghalabat al-zann (predominant opinion). Thus, for rulings based on qiyas, thubut is zanni, not qat'i.
This distinction is crucial for the Hanafi classification of proofs into qat'i and zanni.
4
Understand Taftazani's Critique
Taftazani declares the matn's statement 'la hasil lahu' (has no substance) because the author failed to clarify which definition he meant, leading to confusion. The critique refines the reader's understanding by showing that the matn's claim is ambiguous and can be interpreted in two ways, each with different implications.
This is a methodological flaw in the matn's wording.
5
Apply to the Hanafi Usul Framework
Connect this critique to the broader Hanafi theory of hukm and thubut. The Hanafi school holds that the Quran and Sunnah mutawatir are qat'i al-thubut, while khabar wahid and qiyas are zanni. This distinction affects how rulings are derived and which proofs are considered definitive.
This lesson reinforces the importance of precise terminology in usul.

قوله ان اريد بالحكم هذا كلام لا حاصل له غرض شارح تفتازانی حسب عادت مصنف پر اشکال وارد کرتا ہے کہ مصنف نے جو متن میں یہ کلام کی ہے کہ اگر حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ ہو تو ثبوت حکم سے مراد ثبوت حکم من الادلہ باعتبار علمنا ہوگا نہ کہ نفس الامر اور واقع میں کیونکہ خطاب اللہ قدیم ہے وہ کسی چیز سے ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا اگر حکم کا معنی ما ثبت بالخطاب ہو تو ثبوت علم سے مراد غلبہ ظن ہوگا کیونکہ اگر ثبوت نفس الامری مراد لیا جائے تو ادلہ ثلاثہ ( کتاب سنت اجماع) تو حکم کیلئے مثبت ہو سکتے ہیں قیاس مثبت نہیں بلکہ
His saying: 'If by hukm is meant...' This speech has no substance. The purpose of Sharh Taftazani, according to his habit, is to object to the author. The author said in the matn: If by hukm is meant the address of Allah, then the proof of the ruling means the proof of the ruling from the proofs with respect to our knowledge, not in reality and actuality, because the address of Allah is eternal; it cannot be proven by anything. If the meaning of hukm is 'what is established by the address' (ma thabat bi al-khitab), then the proof of knowledge means predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) because if proof in reality is meant, then the three proofs (Book, Sunnah, Ijma) can establish the ruling, but analogy (qiyas) does not establish it...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by Taftazani on the matn of al-Tawdih. He finds the author's statement about the meaning of 'hukm' and 'thubut' (proof) to be problematic (not fruitful). The issue is: if hukm is defined as Allah's address (khitab Allah), then being proven by evidences only means we know about it, because Allah's address is eternal and not dependent on proofs. If hukm is defined as what is established by the address (ma thabat bi al-khitab), then 'thubut' in the sense of proof refers to ghalabat al-zann (predominant opinion) because for the three main proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) they provide certain evidence, but qiyas does not provide certainty. The passage is incomplete but shows Taftazani's critique.

Key Terms
خطاب اللہ (khitab Allah): The address of Allah; the divine speech
غلبہ ظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion; a level of certainty below absolute certainty
ثبوت (thubut): Proof, establishment; the epistemological status of a ruling or text
حکم (hukm): Ruling, either the divine address or the derived law

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Taftazani's critique, if hukm means 'what is established by the address', then what does 'thubut' from qiyas mean?
A) Certain knowledge (qat')
B) Predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann)
C) Pure speculation (wahm)
D) Contradiction (ta'arud)

Key Takeaway
Precise definition of hukm is essential: either as eternal address (ontological) or derived ruling (epistemological), affecting the certainty of proofs.

Shar'i Proofs Yield Certainty: Refuting the Conjecture Claim
Refuting philosophical claim that shar'i proofs are conjectural

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why Hanafis consider shar'i proofs (Qur'an, mutawatir, mashhur) as yielding certainty (yaqin) and refute the claim that they are only conjectural using the author's argument from punishment.

Core Idea
Shar'i proofs from Qur'an and mutawatir/mashhur hadith produce certainty; their deniers face eternal punishment, proving their binding authority.

This passage is an expansion (sharh) that rebukes a commentator's claim that shar'i proofs are merely indicators (amarat) that do not establish rulings with certainty. The author affirms that the foundational sources—Qur'an, mutawatir hadith, and mashhur hadith—are real proofs and yield yaqin. He grounds this in both a detailed analysis of how rulings are attributed to proofs and a theological argument: if these proofs were merely conjectural, Allah—who is just and merciful—would not prescribe eternal Hell for their denial. This lesson unpacks the logical structure of the author's refutation and its implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim Being Refuted
The commentator (and philosophers) claim that shar'i proofs, unlike logical proofs, are not real proofs; they only produce conjecture (zann) and do not establish rulings in reality. Find where this claim is stated and paraphrased in the passage.
Look for phrases like 'دلائل شرعیہ صرف امارات ہیں' (shar'i proofs are only indicators).
2
Follow the Author's Distinction of Two Meanings of 'Ruling'
The author explains that 'ruling' (hukm) has two senses: (1) the address of Allah (khatab), and (2) what is established by that address. In the first sense, proofs give knowledge ('ilm) directly; in the second, proofs give preponderance (ghalaba). This clarifies how attribution works.
This distinction shows that the philosopher's blanket denial of certainty is based on mixing the two senses.
3
Understand the Author's Core Evidence: Punishment Indicates Certainty
The author argues: if shar'i proofs were only conjectural, then denial would be a minor error, yet Allah threatens eternal Hell for those who reject them. Since Allah is just and merciful, this severe punishment proves that the proofs are certain and binding.
This is a theological argument (dalil naqli) rooted in Allah's attributes.
4
Evaluate the Philosophical Counterposition
The passage labels the philosophical claim as a 'calculated conspiracy' to weaken religion. While strong language, the usul point is that the philosophers' reliance on rational proofs over naqli proofs is invalid because the foundational shar'i proofs are certain.
This underscores the Hanafi stance that the primary sources are qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ماضی بھی بھول جاتے ہیں کیونکہ قبل از این خود آپ یہ عبارت تحریر کر چکے ہیں۔ ثم الثلاثة الأول اصول مطلقة لكونها ادلة مستقلة مثبتة للاحكام الخ فى تفتازاني ماذکرہ من قبل نیز ہم یہ عرض کرتے ہیں کہ تحقیق مصنف مفید ہے کیونکہ مصنف کی تحقیق دو امرین پر مبنی ہے پہلی بات تو یہ ہے احکام کی نسبت ادلہ شرعیہ کی طرف ہوتی ہے ثبوتا وانتفاء مقصد یہ ہے کہ عرف فقہاء و اصولیین میں ادلہ شرعیہ کو ثبت احکام اور نانی لا حکام کہا جاتا ہے (۲) دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ثبوت حکم سے مراد ثبوت نفس الامری (حقیقی) اور واقعی نہیں ہے بلکہ ثبوت فی الجملہ ہے ان دو باتوں سے اتنی بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ حکم کی نسبت ہوتی ہے ادلہ کی طرف اب سوال یہ پیدا ہو حکم کا ثبوت ادلہ سے کس طریقہ پر ہوتا ہے اس کی تفصیل کی ضرورت تھی مصنف نے وہی تحقیق و تفصیل بیان فرمائی کہ اگر حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ ہو تو ثبوت حکم من ادلہ سے مراد ثبوت علم ہوگا اور اگر حکم بمعنی ما ثبت بالخطاب ہو تو ثبوت حکم سے مراد غلبہ کن ہوگا لہذا مصنف کی یہ ساری بحث اور کلام مفید ہے نیز شارح کا یہ دعوی کہ دلائل شرعیہ صرف امارات ہیں مفید ثبوت حکم نہیں ہیں یہ غلط ہے بلکہ یہ اہل فلسفہ کا چھوڑا ہوا شوشہ ہے وہ اپنے ادلہ کو قومی کرنے اور ادلہ شرعیہ کو کمزور کرنے کیلئے کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے اولہ تو مثبتہ ہیں لیکن ادلہ شرعیہ ادلہ حقیقیہ نہیں، ہیں اور نہ ہی وہ مفید لثبوت الحکم فی الواقع ہیں بلکہ وہ صرف ظن کا فائدہ دیتی ہیں یہ سب کچھ انہوں نے سوچی سمجھی سازش کے تحت پرو پیگنڈہ کیا تا کہ ادلہ شرعیہ کو کمزور کیا جا سکے لیکن ہمارا ایمان ہے دلائل شرعیہ قرآن وسنت خصوصاً احادیث متواترہ اور احادیث مشہورہ ادلہ حقیقیہ ہیں مثبتہ الا حکام اور مفید یقین ہیں اسی وجہ سے ان کا منکر کا فر اور مخلد فی النار ہو گا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ادلہ شرعیہ مفید یقین ہیں اگر ظنی ہوتیں تو اللہ تعالی ان کے انکار پر اتنی بڑی سزا تجویز نہ فرماتے لانہ عادل رحیم لا یظلم علی احدلانہ لیس بظلام العبید ۔
They forget the past as well because before this you yourself have written this sentence. 'Then the first three are absolute principles because they are independent proofs that establish rulings, etc.' from Taftazani as mentioned before. We also submit that the author's research is beneficial because his research is based on two matters. First: rulings are attributed to shar'i proofs in terms of affirmation and negation; the purpose is that in the terminology of jurists and usul scholars, shar'i proofs are called affirmers of rulings and negators of rulings. Second: by affirmation of a ruling is meant not real and actual affirmation in itself, but affirmation in a general sense. From these two points it is established that rulings are attributed to proofs. Now the question arises: in what manner is the ruling established from proofs? Detail was needed; the author presented that research and detail: if ruling means the address of Allah, then establishment of ruling from proofs means establishment of knowledge; if ruling means what is established by the address, then establishment of ruling means preponderance. Therefore all this discussion of the author is beneficial. Also the commentator's claim that shar'i proofs are merely indicators and do not establish rulings is false; rather it is a trick left by the philosophers. To validate their own proofs and weaken shar'i proofs, they say: our proofs are affirmative but shar'i proofs are not real proofs, nor do they establish rulings in reality; rather they only yield conjecture. They did all this propaganda under a calculated conspiracy to weaken shar'i proofs. But our faith is that shar'i proofs—the Quran and Sunnah, especially mutawatir and mashhur hadith—are real proofs, affirmers of rulings, and yield certainty. That is why the denier of them is a disbeliever and will abide in Hellfire forever. From this it becomes known that shar'i proofs yield certainty; if they were conjectural, Allah would not prescribe such severe punishment for their denial because He is just, merciful, and does not wrong anyone—He is not unjust to His servants.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a response to the commentator's claim that shar'i proofs are only indicators (amarat) and do not establish rulings with certainty. The author defends the position that shar'i proofs—especially the Qur'an, mutawatir hadith, and mashhur hadith—are real proofs that produce certainty (yaqin). He argues that if these proofs only produced conjecture, Allah would not punish those who reject them with eternal hellfire, as He is just and merciful. The passage also distinguishes between two meanings of 'ruling': as the address of Allah (khatab) and as what is established by that address; in the first case, proofs give knowledge of the ruling directly; in the second, they give preponderance (ghalaba). The author refutes the philosophical position that demeans shar'i proofs, asserting that such propaganda undermines religion. This is a key usul principle: the authority of shar'i proofs is certain, not merely probable, for the foundational sources.

Key Terms
ادلہ شرعیہ (adillah shari'ah): Shar'i proofs: Qur'an, Sunnah (especially mutawatir and mashhur), and other sources recognized by the Shari'ah.
یقین (yaqin): Certainty; the conviction that cannot be doubted, which shar'i proofs provide.
ظن (zann): Conjecture; probability that does not amount to certainty.
حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ (hukm bi ma'na khitab Allah): Ruling in the sense of the divine address itself; the command or prohibition as uttered by Allah.
ثبوت علم (thubut 'ilm): Establishment of knowledge; meaning that the ruling is known directly from the proof.
غلبہ ظن (ghalaba zann): Preponderance of conjecture; the ruling is established with a strong probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what argument does the author use to prove that shar'i proofs yield certainty (yaqin)?
A) The majority of scholars agree that they are certain.
B) The proofs are based on logical necessity.
C) Denial of these proofs leads to eternal punishment in Hell, which Allah would not prescribe for merely conjectural matters.
D) The proofs are supported by qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Shar'i proofs from the Qur'an, mutawatir hadith, and mashhur hadith are real proofs that yield certainty (yaqin); their authority is not conjectural but binding, as evidenced by the severe punishment for rejection.

Refutation of Taftazani's Arguments for Multiple Subjects in a Single Science
Refutation of Taftazani's arguments for multiple subjects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position that each science has one subject and refute Taftazani's arguments for multiple subjects using the examples of geometry and Arabic sciences.

Core Idea
A science's unity requires a single subject; apparent multiplicity is resolved by identifying the genus or a common relation (idafa).

This lesson examines a critical debate in usul al-fiqh about the subject of a science. The Hanafi author refutes Taftazani's claim that a science can have multiple subjects, using two reductio arguments and clarifying the distinction between a concept and its instances. Understanding this debate sharpens your grasp of how sciences are defined.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on subject unity
Understand that the Hanafi school holds that every science must have one subject (mawdu'), which is a single essence or concept. Apparent multiplicity is resolved by identifying a common relation or genus.
This is a rational principle, not derived from a single text.
2
Analyze Taftazani's first argument from geometry
Taftazani argued that line, surface, and solid body share an essential (dhati), so they can be multiple subjects of geometry. Identify this claim.
He considers these as separate subjects because they share an essential attribute.
3
Apply the Hanafi response: types under a genus
The Hanafi author responds that line, surface, and solid body are types (anwa') of the single subject al-kamm al-muttasil al-qarr al-dhat (continuous quantity). They are not separate subjects.
This mirrors the example from grammar: the subject is kalima, and its types (ism, fi'l, harf) do not multiply the subject.
4
Analyze Taftazani's second argument and the reductio
Taftazani claimed that multiple subjects sharing a common accident could be unified. The Hanafi author uses reductio ad absurdum: if sharing any accident sufficed, fiqh and geometry would be one; if sharing a specific accident sufficed, all Arabic sciences would be one. Both are false.
This logical argument shows the absurdity of Taftazani's criterion.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

پھر یقینا ہر شخص کو حق حاصل ہوگا کہ وہ فقہ اور ہندسہ کو علم واحد قرار دے آپ کس طرح اور کس قانون کے تحت اس کو روکیں گے اعتراض ثالث یہ تھا کہ کلام مصنف میں تضاد و تناقض ہے تو جواب یہ ہے کہ کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے کیونکہ موضوع فن کے مفہوم کے عوارض ذاتیہ فن میں بیان نہیں کیے جاتے بلکہ مفہوم کے جو مصادیق ہوتے ہیں ان کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہوتی ہے مثلا کلمہ نحو کا موضوع ہے اب نحو میں کلمہ کے مفہوم کے عوارض ذاتیہ نہیں بیان کیے جاتے بلکہ اس کے جو مصداق ہیں اسم فعل حرف ان کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی جاتی ہے لیکن اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ اسم فعل، حرف نحو کا موضوع بن جائیں بلکہ موضوع وہی کلمہ ہی ہوگا تو یہ مسلم بات ہے کہ مفہوم موضوع کے عوارض سے بحث نہیں ہوتی بلکہ موضوع کے انواع اور مصادیق کے عوارض سے بحث ہوتی ہے اسی طرح اصول فقہ میں بھی مفہوم دلیل کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کے مصادیق کتاب سنت، اجماع قیاس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہوتی ہے لیکن موضوع پھر بھی دلیل ہو گا نہ کہ کتاب وسنت و غیرہ تو مثال میں بھی تعدد موضوع نہیں ہے اس لئے تناقض و تعارض فی کلام المصنف لازم نہیں آرہا۔
Explanation of al-Tawdih: The second will not, but the knowledge will be one because here it is necessary to make both mudaf (construct) as the subject. So if one is made, then preference without a preponderant would be necessary, and if the conditions and essential accidents of one are interpreted and referred to the other, then that is an unnecessary burden. Therefore both mudafs are made as subjects. Then if looked at, here the subjects are multiple, but in reality the subject is one, which is the relation (idafa) between the mudaf and the mudaf ilayh (between the two mudafs). Therefore when the subject is one, the issues and predicates will also be appropriate and unified because all of them refer to the two parts of this single relation. It is as if all are states of one subject. When the subject and predicate are proportionate, the issues will be unified and proportionate, and due to their unity the knowledge will also be one. Thus the author's statement is proven: the subject of a single science is one. And that which appears as multiplicity in the relation between the two things is only at first glance, but in reality there is no multiplicity; even in that case the subject is one, which is al-idafa. Also the commentator Taftazani, while presenting evidence for multiple subjects, said that line, surface, and solid body (jism ta'limi) share in one essential (dhati), so due to this proportionality multiple subjects are permissible. So the answer is that here Taftazani is mistaken: the subject of geometry is not line, surface, etc., but the subject of geometry is that same essential (al-kamm al-muttasil al-qarr al-dhat). Line, etc., are its types; they are not themselves the subject. And in an art, just as the essential accidents of the subject itself are discussed, similarly the essential accidents of its types are also discussed; this is also in reality a discussion of the essential accidents of the subject. For example, the subject of grammar is kalima, but in grammar the essential accidents of its types—ism, fi'l, harf—are also discussed. From this it does not follow that the subject of grammar is ism, fi'l, harf; rather the subject is kalima, and all these are its types. Similarly, the subject of geometry is one: al-miqdar, i.e., al-kamm al-muttasil al-qarr al-dhat. It is not correct for the commentator to make this an example of multiple subjects. Similarly, the commentator said that if there are multiple subjects and they share in one accident (arad), then multiple subjects are permissible. This is also wrong because we ask: what do you mean by accident? Absolute accident or a specific accident? If you mean absolute accident, then we say that fiqh and geometry should both be considered a single science because the subject of fiqh is the act of the responsible person (fi'l mukallaf) and the subject of geometry is al-kamm al-muttasil al-qarr al-dhat, and these both share in being accidents because fi'l mukallaf is an accident and al-kamm al-muttasil is also an accident—neither is a substance. Therefore these two sciences should be called one science, although no one holds them to be one. And if you mean a specific accident, even then it is not correct because all Arabic sciences—morphology, syntax, prosody, etc.—share in a specific accident, which is that their subject is words. The purpose and goal of all of them is to avoid verbal error. So all these sciences should be called one science because they share in that specific accident, yet that is clearly false. Therefore it is proven that this kind of proportionality is not sufficient for the unity of a science. The answer to the second objection is: if multiple subjects are allowed without any proportionality, then certainly every person would have the right to consider fiqh and geometry as one science. How and under what law would you prevent him? The third objection was that there is contradiction in the author's speech. The answer is that there is no contradiction because in an art, the essential accidents of the concept (mafhum) of the subject are not discussed; rather the discussion is about the essential accidents of the instances (masadiq) of the concept. For example, kalima is the subject of grammar. Now in grammar, the essential accidents of the concept of kalima are not discussed, but the essential accidents of its instances—ism, fi'l, harf—are discussed. But from this it does not follow that ism, fi'l, harf become the subject of grammar; rather the subject remains kalima. So it is accepted that the discussion is not about the accidents of the concept of the subject, but about the accidents of the types and instances of the subject. Similarly, in usul al-fiqh, the discussion is not about the essential accidents of the concept of dalil (evidence), but about the essential accidents of its instances: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas. Yet the subject remains dalil, not Kitab, Sunnah, etc. So in the example as well, there is no multiplicity of subject; therefore contradiction and conflict in the author's speech do not arise.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (haskiya) from the super-commentary Misk al-Malih on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. The author refutes two arguments by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani (the commentator in al-Talwih) in favor of allowing multiple subjects in a single science. The first argument: Taftazani claimed that geometry's subject is line, surface, and solid body, which share an essential (dhati), so multiple subjects are permissible. The author responds that geometry's real subject is al-kamm al-muttasil al-qarr al-dhat (continuous quantity); lines, surfaces, etc. are merely types under it, not separate subjects. The second argument: Taftazani claimed that multiple subjects can be unified if they share a common accident (arad). The author uses a reductio ad absurdum: if sharing any accident suffices, then fiqh and geometry would be one science because both subjects are accidents (acts of the responsible person and continuous quantity are both accidents). If sharing a specific accident suffices, then all Arabic sciences (syntax, morphology, etc.) would be one because their subjects are all words and their goal is avoiding verbal error. Both consequences are false. The author also answers the objection that the author's own statements are contradictory, clarifying the distinction between the concept (mafhum) of a subject and its instances (masadiq). In any art, discussion is about the accidents of instances, not the concept, so the subject remains singular.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science; that which is investigated for its essential accidents.
عرض (arad): An accident; a contingent attribute that is not essential to the substance.
اضافت (idafa): Relation; specifically the grammatical construct (mudaf-mudaf ilayh) used as an example of a single subject underlying apparent multiplicity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the example of line, surface, and solid body not make geometry have multiple subjects?
A) Because they are all accidents
B) Because they are types under one genus (kamm muttasil), not separate subjects
C) Because geometry's subject is actually the act of the responsible person
D) Because Taftazani agreed they are one subject

Key Takeaway
The unity of a science requires a single subject; apparent multiplicity is resolved by identifying the genus or a common relation, such as idafa.

The Hanafi Definition of the Quran and the Refutation of Circularity
Defining the Quran and defending the definition from circularity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran, explain how each qualifier excludes other texts, and refute the objection of circularity by distinguishing between technical and conventional knowledge.

Core Idea
The Quran is the mutawatir text between the covers of the mus'haf; the circularity objection fails because 'mus'haf' is conventionally understood.

This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi definition of the Quran used in usul al-fiqh. We examine the precise wording, the function of each condition, and then tackle a famous logical objection raised by Ibn al-Hajib. Understanding this definition is foundational for recognizing the Quran as the first and primary source of Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition and Its Components
Locate the full definition in the passage: 'It is that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'haf by tawatur.' Break it into parts: (a) transmitted to us, (b) between the two covers, (c) of the mus'haf, (d) by tawatur.
Each part has a specific excluding function.
2
Understand What Each Qualifier Excludes
Map each qualifier to what it excludes: 'between the two covers' excludes other scriptures (Torah, Injil), divine hadith (qudsi), and prophetic hadith. 'By tawatur' excludes irregular recitations (qira'at shadhdhah) that are not mass-transmitted.
This shows the precision of the definition.
3
Grasp Ibn al-Hajib's Objection (Dawr)
Ibn al-Hajib argued that the definition is circular: knowledge of the Quran depends on knowledge of the mus'haf, but knowledge of the mus'haf would require knowing the Quran (since a mus'haf is defined as 'that in which the Quran is written').
Circularity would make the definition invalid.
4
Learn the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response has two parts: First, the term 'mus'haf' is conventionally known among the people and needs no technical definition. Second, a more detailed investigation (hinted at) shows that the knowledge of the mus'haf does not actually depend on a formal definition of the Quran; common recognition suffices.
Thus, no circularity arises because the definition uses a term understood by common practice ('urf).
5
Apply the Distinction Between Technical and Conventional Knowledge
Recognize that in usul al-fiqh, definitions may rely on terms that are well-known by convention even if they are not formally defined. This is a legitimate technique to avoid infinite regress or circularity.
This principle appears in many definitions throughout Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنضع الكتاب علی قسمین مصنف فرماتے ہیں ہم اس کتاب کو دو فلمیں پر وضع کر رہے ہیں قسم اول اولہ شرعیہ میں اور قسم ثانی احکام میں ہے پھر ادلہ شرعیہ چار ارکان پر مشتمل ہیں کتاب سنت، اجماع، قیاس ، رکن اول کتاب میں ہے ای القرآن یہ تفسیر ہے الکتاب کی بلفظ اشھر اس کو تعریف لفظی کہا جاتا ہے، وھو ما نقل الینا بین وقتی المصاحف تو اترا، یہ قرآن پاک کی تعریف حقیقی ہے دفتین بمعنی جانیں حاصل تعریف یہ ہے کہ کتاب ( قرآن ) وہ ہے جو مصاحف کے دو گتوں کے درمیان ہماری طرف نقل کیا گیا ہے تو اتر کے ساتھ مصاحف سے وہ مصاحف مراد ہیں جو حضرت عثمان رضی اللہ عنہ نے جمع کرائے پھر ان کے بعد جو ان کے موافق ہو کر پھیلے فخرج سائر الکتاب یہاں سے فوائد قیود بیان کر رہے ہیں رفتی المصاحف فصل اول ہے اس سے (۱) باقی کتب الہیہ خارج ہو گئیں تو راہ انجیل و غیر ها (۲) احادیث الہیہ ( قدسیہ ) خارج ہو گئیں (ب) احادیث نبویه ای اقوال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم وافعال واحوالہ خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ یہ تمام منقول بین دفتی المصاحف نہیں ہیں، تو اتر افصل ثانی ہے اس سے قرآة شاذہ خارج ہوگئی کیونکہ یہ منقول الینا بالتواتر نہیں ہے بلکہ بعض مصاحف مخصوصہ میں ہے مثلا مصحف ابن مسعود صحف ابی بن کعب ان کی نقل بالتواتر نہیں بلکہ باخبار الا حاد ہے وقد اورد ابن الحاجب ان هذا . التعريف دوری مصنف علامہ ابن حاجب کا اعتراض نقل کر کے اس کے دو جوابات دے رہے ہیں علامہ ابن الحاجب نے اشکال کیا ہے کہ اس تعریف میں دور لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ کتاب کی تعریف کی گئی مانقل الینا بین وقتی المصحف تو معرفت قرآن موقوف ہوگی معرفت مصحف پر کیونکہ معرف موقوف ہوتا ہے علی معرفہ اجزاء التعریف لہذا تعریف مصحف ضروری ہے ورنہ ما ہیت قرآن واضح نہیں ہو گی اب اگر مصحف کے بارے میں سوال کیا جائے ما المصحف ؟ تو لا محالہ جواب یہ ہو گا الذی كتب فيه القرآن و معرفت مصحف موقوف ہوگئی معرفت کتاب (قرآن) پر اسی کو دور کہا جاتا ہے ای توقف الشئى على ما يتوقف عليه ذالك الشئى فاجبت عن هذا بقولی جواب ! مصنف نے جواب دیا کہ یہاں کوئی دور نہیں ہے کیونکہ کتاب (قرآن) کی تعریف تو موقوف علی معرفۃ المصحف ہے لیکن مصحف کی معرفت قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہے کیونکہ مصحف کی تعریف کرنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ مصحف معلوم و متعارف بین الناس ہے لوگ جانتے پہچانتے ہیں اس لئے یہ محتاج الی التعریف نہیں ہے تو معرفت قرآن تو موقوف على معرفۃ المصحف ہے ولکن لا يتوقف معرفة المصحف على معرفة القرآن فلا دور - ثم أردت تحقيقا في هذا الموضع الخ یہاں سے مصنف اعتراض ابن الحاجب کا دوسرا جواب دے رہے ہیں جواب سے قبل تمہید بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ میں اس مقام تعریف میں کچھ تحقیق کرنا
So we place the book into two divisions: the author says we are placing this book into two parts: the first division is in rulings (shar'iyyah) and the second in commands (ahkam). Then the shar'i proofs consist of four pillars: Book, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas. The first pillar is the Book, i.e., the Quran. This is an interpretation of 'al-Kitab' by the more famous word. This is called a verbal definition. 'It is that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'haf by tawatur.' This is the real definition of the Holy Quran. 'daffatayn' meaning two covers. So the full definition is: The Book (Quran) is that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'haf by tawatur. By 'mus'haf' are meant the mus'hafs that 'Uthman (RA) collected and then spread in agreement with them. ... Then Ibn al-Hajib raised an objection that this definition involves circularity (dawr) because knowledge of the Quran depends on knowledge of the mus'haf, and knowledge of the mus'haf depends on knowledge of the Quran. The author gives two answers: first, the mus'haf is known by common knowledge and needs no definition; second, he proceeds to present a more detailed investigation.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of the Quran from the matn (Al-Tawdih). The author divides the book into two parts: one on the proofs (adillah) and one on the rulings (ahkam). The first proof is the Quran. It is defined as 'that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'haf by tawatur.' This is a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi). The commentator explains each phrase: 'between the two covers' excludes other scriptures (like Injil), divine hadith (hadith qudsi), and prophetic hadith. 'By tawatur' excludes irregular recitations (qira'at shadhdhah). Then the commentator cites an objection by Ibn al-Hajib: the definition is circular because it defines 'kitab' using 'mus'haf', and then 'mus'haf' would be defined using 'kitab'. The response is that no circularity exists because the knowledge of 'mus'haf' is taken as commonly known (ma'rifat al-mushaf ghayr mawqufah 'ala al-qur'an); the term 'mus'haf' is conventionally understood among people and needs no formal definition. Finally, the commentator hints at a second, more detailed answer to be given later.

Key Terms
الکتاب (al-kitab): The Quran, defined as the mutawatir transmitted text between the covers of the 'Uthmanic mus'haf
مصحف (mus'haf): The codex containing the Quranic text, specifically the 'Uthmanic copies
تواتر (tawatur): Transmission by a large number of narrators such that collusion on a lie is impossible, giving certain knowledge

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is excluded from the definition of the Quran by the condition 'transmitted by tawatur'?
A) The prophetic hadith
B) The irregular recitations (qira'at shadhdhah)
C) The divine hadith (hadith qudsi)
D) The previous scriptures like the Torah and Injil

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran is precise and defensible; the charge of circularity is resolved by recognizing that 'mus'haf' is a term of common knowledge, not a technical definition that would cause a regress.

The Hanafi Definition of the Quran and Its Conditions
Definition of Quran with conditions and exclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran and identify which categories of divine speech are excluded by each of its two conditions.

Core Idea
The Quran is defined by its written, mass-transmitted text — not by its divine origin alone.

In Hanafi usul, the definition of the Quran is not merely theoretical; it determines which texts are legally binding for deriving rulings. The standard definition – 'that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mushafs, mutawatir' – carefully excludes other forms of divine speech. This lesson unpacks the definition and explains why each component is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
The definition has two key parts: (1) transmitted between the covers of the mushafs, (2) transmitted mutawatir. Each condition serves a specific exclusion.
The definition is often cited in Hanafi works; note its function to isolate the Quran from other speech.
2
Analyse 'between the covers of the mushafs'
This condition excludes previous scriptures (Torah, Injil), hadith qudsi, and prophetic hadith (sayings, actions, states). These are not physically collected in the standard mushaf.
Even hadith qudsi, though divine in meaning, is excluded because it was not transmitted as part of the Quranic text.
3
Analyse 'mutawatir'
This condition excludes irregular (shadhdh) recitations that are not mass-transmitted. Only the universally accepted text (qira'at mutawatira) qualifies.
Recitations like those of Ibn Mas'ud or Ubayy ibn Ka'b that reached us via ahad reports are not included.
4
Summarise the exclusions
Compile a clear list of what is not Quran: other divine books, hadith qudsi, prophetic hadith, and shadhdh recitations. Understand the basis: either lack of physical collection or lack of tawatur.
This establishes the Quran as a distinct, defined corpus for legal inference.

فنضع الكتاب علی قسمین مصنف فرماتے ہیں ہم اس کتاب کو دو فلمیں پر وضع کر رہے ہیں قسم اول اولہ شرعیہ میں اور قسم ثانی احکام میں ہے پھر ادلہ شرعیہ چار ارکان پر مشتمل ہیں کتاب سنت، اجماع، قیاس ، رکن اول کتاب میں ہے ای القرآن یہ تفسیر ہے الکتاب کی بلفظ اشھر اس کو تعریف لفظی کہا جاتا ہے، وھو ما نقل الینا بین وقتی المصاحف تو اترا، یہ قرآن پاک کی تعریف حقیقی ہے دفتین بمعنی جانیں حاصل تعریف یہ ہے کہ کتاب ( قرآن ) وہ ہے جو مصاحف کے دو گتوں کے درمیان ہماری طرف نقل کیا گیا ہے تو اتر کے ساتھ مصاحف سے وہ مصاحف مراد ہیں جو حضرت عثمان رضی اللہ عنہ نے جمع کرائے پھر ان کے بعد جو ان کے موافق ہو کر پھیلے فخرج سائر الکتاب یہاں سے فوائد قیود بیان کر رہے ہیں رفتی المصاحف فصل اول ہے اس سے (۱) باقی کتب الہیہ خارج ہو گئیں تو راہ انجیل و غیر ها (۲) احادیث الہیہ ( قدسیہ ) خارج ہو گئیں (ب) احادیث نبویه ای اقوال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم وافعال واحوالہ خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ یہ تمام منقول بین دفتی المصاحف نہیں ہیں، تو اتر افصل ثانی ہے اس سے قرآة شاذہ خارج ہوگئی کیونکہ یہ منقول الینا بالتواتر نہیں ہے بلکہ بعض مصاحف مخصوصہ میں ہے مثلا مصحف ابن مسعود صحف ابی بن کعب ان کی نقل بالتواتر نہیں بلکہ باخبار الا حاد ہے وقد اورد ابن الحاجب ان هذا . التعريف دوری مصنف علامہ ابن حاجب کا اعتراض نقل کر کے اس کے دو جوابات دے رہے ہیں علامہ ابن الحاجب نے اشکال کیا ہے کہ اس تعریف میں دور لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ کتاب کی تعریف کی گئی مانقل الینا بین وقتی المصحف تو معرفت قرآن موقوف ہوگی معرفت مصحف پر کیونکہ معرف موقوف ہوتا ہے علی معرفہ اجزاء التعریف لہذا تعریف مصحف ضروری ہے ورنہ ما ہیت قرآن واضح نہیں ہو گی اب اگر مصحف کے بارے میں سوال کیا جائے ما المصحف ؟ تو لا محالہ جواب یہ ہو گا الذی كتب فيه القرآن و معرفت مصحف موقوف ہوگئی معرفت کتاب (قرآن) پر اسی کو دور کہا جاتا ہے ای توقف الشئى على ما يتوقف عليه ذالك الشئى فاجبت عن هذا بقولی جواب ! مصنف نے جواب دیا کہ یہاں کوئی دور نہیں ہے کیونکہ کتاب (قرآن) کی تعریف تو موقوف علی معرفۃ المصحف ہے لیکن مصحف کی معرفت قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہے کیونکہ مصحف کی تعریف کرنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ مصحف معلوم و متعارف بین الناس ہے لوگ جانتے پہچانتے ہیں اس لئے یہ محتاج الی التعریف نہیں ہے تو معرفت قرآن تو موقوف على معرفۃ المصحف ہے ولکن لا يتوقف معرفة المصحف على معرفة القرآن فلا دور - ثم أردت تحقيقا في هذا الموضع الخ یہاں سے مصنف اعتراض ابن الحاجب کا دوسرا جواب دے رہے ہیں جواب سے قبل تمہید بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ میں اس مقام تعریف میں کچھ تحقیق کرنا
